Wiping the Ears: Sunnah Method
Ruling on wiping ears: Sunnah, method, and condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Sunnah ruling on wiping the ears in wudu, describe the chosen method, and apply the condition of baqa' al-ballah.

Core Idea
Wiping the ears is Sunnah even with leftover head water, but moisture must remain; else renew.

The ears are an integral part of wudu, but their wiping is Sunnah, not obligatory. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi outlines the preferred method and the crucial condition of moisture. Understanding this dispels the misconception that fresh water is always required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Confirm that wiping the ears during wudu is a Sunnah act (not fard or wajib). The text states 'yusann' (it is Sunnah).
This is established from the Prophet's practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the prophetic action: the Prophet cupped a handful of water, wiped his head, and then wiped his ears with the same water.
The hadith is not quoted but referenced implicitly.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action demonstrates that using leftover water is permissible and Sunnah; the method is derived from his practice.
The command to wipe the head is general; the ears are included through the prophetic model.
4
Examine the chosen method
The preferred method (al-mukhtar) is to wipe the outer ears with the thumbs, the inner ears with the index fingers, and insert the little fingers into the ear holes and move them.
This is from al-Mi'raj and transmitted by al-Halwani and Shaykh al-Islam.
5
Apply the condition of baqa' al-ballah
The Sunnah is fulfilled with leftover water only if moisture remains. If the moisture is gone (e.g., dried on the hand), fresh water must be taken to fulfill the Sunnah.
If moisture is absent, wiping without renewal does not earn the Sunnah reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسن مسح الأذنين ولو بماء الرأس لأنه غرف غرفة فمسح بها رأسه وأذنيه فإن أخذ لهما ماء جديد بقاء البلة كان حسنا. قوله: الأذنين بأن يمسح ظاهرهما بالإبهامين وداخلهما بالسبابتين وهو المختار كما في المعراج ويدخل الخنصرين في حجريهما ويحركهما كما في البحر عن الحلواني وشيخ الإسلام. قوله: (مع بقاء البلة) أما فنائها بأن رفع العمامة بهما فلا يكون مقيماً للسنة إلا بالتجديد.
And it is Sunnah to wipe the ears, even with the water of the head, because he cupped a handful and wiped his head and his ears. If he takes fresh water for them while moisture remains, it is good. He said: (the ears) i.e., he wipes their exteriors with the thumbs and their interiors with the index fingers, and that is the chosen view as in al-Mi'raj, and he inserts the little fingers into the ear holes and moves them as in al-Bahr from al-Halwani and Shaykh al-Islam. He said: (with remaining moisture) as for its disappearance, like if he lifts the turban with them, then he is not fulfilling the Sunnah except with renewal.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the Sunnah of wiping the ears during wudu. The matn states that it is Sunnah to wipe the ears, even if using the leftover water from wiping the head, because the Prophet cupped a handful of water, wiped his head, and then wiped his ears with the same water. However, if one takes fresh water while the moisture from the head remains, it is also fine. The Hashiya expands on the method: the preferred way (al-mukhtar) is to wipe the outer part of the ears with the thumbs and the inner part with the index fingers, and to insert the little fingers into the ear holes and move them, as narrated from al-Halwani and Shaykh al-Islam. It also clarifies the condition 'with remaining moisture': if the moisture is gone (e.g., the turban dried it), one must renew the water to fulfill the Sunnah.

Key Terms
بقاء البلة (baqa' al-ballah): Remaining moisture on the hand from previous wiping
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen/relied-upon method

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How are the ears wiped according to the chosen method in the Hashiya?
A) Wipe only the outside with the index fingers
B) Wipe the outside with thumbs, inside with index fingers, and insert little fingers in holes
C) Wipe with all fingers together
D) Wipe only the inside with the little fingers

Key Takeaway
Wiping the ears is a Sunnah act in wudu that can be performed with the leftover water from the head, provided moisture remains, following the prescribed method.

The Ruling and Definition of Dalk (Rubbing) in Wudu
Ruling on rubbing limbs in wudu and its definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dalk (rubbing) in wudu and ghusl, define it precisely, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Maliki position.

Core Idea
Rubbing (dalk) in wudu is sunnah, not fard or wajib — omitting it does not invalidate wudu.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies that dalk (rubbing) during wudu is a recommended act (sunnah), not an obligatory one. It provides a precise definition and contrasts the Hanafi ruling with that of Imam Malik and al-Awza'i, who consider dalk a condition for validity. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying Hanafi fiqh in daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the ruling on dalk in the text. The matn explicitly says 'and it is Sunnah to rub' and later 'rubbing is not fard'. The ruling is sunnah (recommended).
Note that the Hanafi school places dalk as sunnah, not obligatory.
2
Define the term dalk precisely
The Hashiya defines dalk as 'passing the hand over the limb with flowing of water'. This is a technical definition specific to wudu and ghusl.
Some authorities specify that dalk refers to the first wash only, as indicated by Ibn Amir Hajj's comment.
3
Contrast with the Maliki position
The text notes that Malik and al-Awza'i consider dalk a condition (shart) for validity. Identify the practical difference: for a Hanafi, omitting dalk leaves wudu valid but incomplete in sunnah; for a Maliki, wudu is invalid.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (scholarly difference) with evidence on both sides.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسن الدلك مع الفعل بعده بإمرار يده على الأعضاء. قوله: (الدلك) هو إمرار اليد على العضو مع إسالة الماء ذكره الحموي في بحث الغسل، وفي النهر عن منية المصلي هو إمرار اليد على الأعضاء المغسولة في المرة الأولى اهـ قال ابن أمير حاج لعلى التقييد بالمرة الأولى اتفاقي مع أنها سابقة في الوجود على ما بعدها فهي به أولى لأن السبق من أسباب الترجيح اهـ وليس الدلك فرضاً لا عند مالك والأوزاعي فإنهما شرطاه في صحة الوضوء والغسل.
And it is Sunnah to rub, along with the action after it, by passing his hand over the limbs. He said: (rubbing) is passing the hand over the limb with flowing of water, mentioned by al-Hamawi in the discussion of ghusl. And in al-Nahr from Munyat al-Musalli: it is passing the hand over the washed limbs in the first time. End. Ibn Amir Hajj said: perhaps the restriction to the first time is agreed upon, and it (the first time) precedes what is after it, so it is more appropriate because precedence is one of the reasons for preference. End. And rubbing is not fard, unlike according to Malik and al-Awza'i, for they made it a condition for the validity of wudu and ghusl.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This is a definition and ruling on dalk (rubbing) in wudu and ghusl. The matn states that dalk is sunnah, to be done after washing by passing the hand over the limbs. The Hashiya defines dalk as passing the hand over the limb while water is flowing. It notes that according to some sources, dalk specifically refers to the first wash only, because the first wash is the primary one. Importantly, the text clarifies that dalk is not fard (obligatory) unlike the position of Malik and al-Awza'i who consider it a condition for validity. In the Hanafi school, it is merely a sunnah; omitting it does not invalidate wudu or ghusl.

Key Terms
الدلك (al-dalk): Passing the hand over the limb while water flows (rubbing)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hashiya, what is the ruling of dalk (rubbing) in Hanafi fiqh?
A) It is fard (obligatory)
B) It is sunnah (recommended)
C) It is makruh (disliked)
D) It is haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, drying/rubbing (dalk) in wudu is a sunnah — recommended but not required for validity.

Muwalah in Wudu: Sunnah, Definition, and Conditions
Ruling on consecutiveness in wudu with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define muwalah, state its ruling as sunnah, and identify the conditions and excuses that affect its application.

Core Idea
Muwalah is sunnah: wash the next limb before the previous one dries, considering normal body, time, and place.

The Hanafi school holds that consecutiveness (muwalah) in wudu is a sunnah, not an obligatory element. This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi refines the definition and clarifies the conditions under which it is considered to be observed or excused. Understanding these nuances prevents unnecessary scrupulosity and ensures proper practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling of Muwalah
The passage begins by stating that muwalah is sunnah. Note the word 'yusannu' (it is sunnah) – this is the legal classification.
In Hanafi fiqh, sunnah mu'akkadah is a recommended act that the Prophet ﷺ consistently performed.
2
Define Muwalah as per the Text
The text defines muwalah as 'washing the limbs before the previous one dries with moderation of body, time, and place.' Focus on the two key components: immediacy (before drying) and normalcy (i'tidal).
Two interpretations of 'before previous dries' are mentioned: one considers the first limb dried, the other considers the immediate previous limb.
3
Understand the Condition of I'tidal
I'tidal refers to normal conditions of body (e.g., not excessively absorbent skin), time (e.g., not extremely hot), and place (e.g., not a dry windy area). If these conditions are abnormal, the requirement of muwalah is relaxed.
If the body or environment causes rapid drying, one is not considered to have left muwalah even if a limb dries before washing the next.
4
Apply the Excusing Factors
If the skin absorbs water quickly or the air/place is hot, then even if a limb dries before the next is washed, muwalah is still considered fulfilled. Conversely, if the skin stays wet for a long time due to humidity, failing to wash quickly does break the sunnah.
The criterion is whether the delay is due to external factors or lack of diligence.
5
Note Practical Rulings on Drying Limbs
Drying a limb intentionally before completing wudu (e.g., drying arms before washing feet) is disliked because it breaks the sunnah of muwalah. After finishing wudu, drying is fine.
This highlights that muwalah applies throughout the wudu act, not just between obligatory parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسن الولاء لمواظبته وهو بكسر الواو المتابعة بغسل الأعضاء قبل جفاف السابق مع الاعتدال جسدا وزماناً ومكاناً. قوله: (قبل جفاف السابق) بأن يغسل الأخير قبل جفاف الأول. وفي السيد تبعاً للشارح هو أن يغسل العضو الثاني قبل جفاف الأول اهـ فاعتبر الأول لا الآخر السابق وهما طريقتان. وفي المعراج عن الحلواني تجفيف الأعضاء قبل غسل القدمين لا يفعل لأن فيه ترك الولاء. قال في البحر أي بخلافه بعد الفراغ فإنه لا بأس. ويتحقق الولاء في الفرائض والسنن كما أفاده السيد متعقباً للحموي في إفادته قصره على الفرائض. قوله: (مع الاعتدال جسداً وزماناً ومكاناً) فلو كان بدنه يتشرب الماء أو كان الهواء شديداً، أو كان المكان حاراً يجفف الماء سريعاً، فلا يعد تاركاً له ولو كان طرياً لا يجففه إلا في مدة مستطيلة، وتأتي في الوضوء لا يكون آنياً بسنة الولاء.
And it is Sunnah to perform consecutively due to his constancy on it, and it (al-wala') is, with kasr of the waw, the following up by washing the limbs before drying of the previous one, with moderation of body, time, and place. He said: (before drying of the previous) i.e., he washes the last before the first dries. And in al-Sayyid following the commentator: it is that he washes the second limb before the first dries. End. So he considered the first, not the other previous one, and they are two methods. And in al-Mi'raj from al-Halwani: drying the limbs before washing the feet is not done because it involves leaving the consecutiveness. He said in al-Bahr: i.e., contrary to after finishing, for then it is no problem. And consecutiveness is realized in the obligatory and the supererogatory acts, as al-Sayyid stated following al-Hamawi in his statement limiting it to obligatory. He said: (with moderation of body, time, and place) so if his body absorbs water, or the air is strong, or the place is hot so that it dries quickly, then he is not considered to be leaving it. And if it is moist that does not dry except in a long period, and it occurs in wudu, it is not immediate with the sunnah of consecutiveness.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This is a ruling on muwalah (consecutiveness) in wudu. The matn states that it is Sunnah to wash the limbs consecutively without delay, defined as washing the next limb before the previous one dries, considering normal conditions of body, time, and place. The Hashiya elaborates: there are two interpretations of 'before drying of the previous' — some say 'last before first dries,' others say 'second before first dries,' but both basically require washing before the first limb dries. The commentary adds that it is disliked to intentionally dry limbs before completing wudu (like drying arms before washing feet) because that breaks consecutiveness. However, after finishing wudu, drying is fine. Muwalah applies to both faraid (obligatory parts) and sunnan (sunnah acts), contrary to a view limiting it to faraid. The condition of 'moderation' means if external factors (like hot climate or dry skin) cause quick drying, one is not considered to have left muwalah. Conversely, if the skin stays wet for a long time (e.g., humid conditions), then failing to wash quickly may still break the sunnah if one delays unnecessarily.

Key Terms
الولاء (al-wala'): Consecutiveness: washing subsequent limbs before previous ones dry
الاعتدال (al-i'tidal): Normal condition of body, time, and place
تجفيف الأعضاء (tajfif al-a'da'): Drying the limbs intentionally with a towel or cloth before completing wudu

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the definition of muwalah in wudu?
A) Washing the limbs in a fixed order without any interruption.
B) Washing each limb before the previously washed limb dries, under normal conditions.
C) Washing the limbs quickly without pausing for any reason.
D) Drying each limb immediately after washing it.

Key Takeaway
Muwalah in wudu is a sunnah defined as washing limbs before the previous one dries, but it is excused when external factors cause rapid drying.

Niyyah (Intention) in Wudu: Definition and Ruling
Definition and ruling on intention in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of niyyah, explain why it is sunnah in wudu but fard in tayammum, and identify the evidence from Quran and Sunnah that supports the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Intention is a heart action; in wudu it is sunnah, not fard, because neither Quran nor Sunnah require it.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi defines niyyah (intention) and clarifies its ruling in wudu. Understanding why it is sunnah in wudu but fard in tayammum is key to appreciating the Hanafi method of deriving rulings from textual evidence and the role of intention in purification.

Guided Path
1
Define niyyah and identify its ruling
Read the definition of niyyah linguistically and terminologically. Note that the ruling in wudu is sunnah, not fard.
The text explicitly states 'ويسن النية' (it is sunnah to intend).
2
Analyze the evidence for the ruling
Examine the Quranic verse (wudu ayah) which commands only washing and wiping without mentioning intention. Then recall the Prophet’s teaching to the bedouin who did not mention intention. Both proofs indicate intention is not obligatory for wudu.
The dalil is dalala zanniyya; it is not explicitly negated, but absence in the verse and prophetic practice supports the Hanafi view.
3
Compare with tayammum
Note that niyyah is fard in tayammum because tayammum uses earth, which is not inherently purifying. Intention distinguishes it from mere dust.
The text says: 'وفرضت في التيمم لأنه بالتراب وليس مزيلاً للحدث بالأصالة' (it is made fard in tayammum because it is with earth and not originally remover of impurity).
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Identify that some Hanafis (like al-Quduri) consider it mustahabb, while the relied-upon position is sunnah. Compare with Shafi'is who consider it fard in wudu.
The cross-madhhab difference is based on different interpretations of the hadith 'Actions are by intentions'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسن النية وهي لغة عزم القلب على الفعل واصطلاحاً توجه القلب لايجاد الفعل جزماً ووقتها قبل الاستنجاء ليكون جميع فعله قربة وكيفيتها أن ينوي رفع الحدث أو إقامة الصلاة أو ينوي الوضوء أو امتثال الأمر ومحلها القلب فإن نطق بها ليجمع بين فعل القلب واللسان استحبه المشايخ والنية سنة لتحصيل الثواب لأن المأمور به ليس إلا غسلاً ومسحاً في الآية ولم يعلمه النبي للاعرابي مع جهله وفرضت في التيمم لأنه بالتراب وليس مزيلاً للحدث بالأصالة.
And it is Sunnah to make intention, and it is, in language, the resolve of the heart to do an action; and in terminology, the heart's direction to definitely produce the action. Its time is before istinja' so that all his action is devotion. Its manner is that he intends to remove impurity, or to perform prayer, or intends wudu, or compliance with the command. Its place is the heart. If he utters it to combine both heart and tongue, the mashayikh considered it good. And intention is Sunnah to attain reward, because the commanded is only washing and wiping in the verse, and the Prophet did not teach it to the bedouin, despite his ignorance, and it is made fard in tayammum because it is with earth and not originally remover of impurity.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This is a definition and ruling on niyyah (intention) in wudu. The matn states that intention is Sunnah, not fard. The Hashiya defines niyyah linguistically and terminologically, emphasizing that it is a resolve of the heart. The time for intention is before istinja' (cleansing after relieving oneself) so that all actions become acts of worship (qurbah). The intention can be expressed by intending to remove ritual impurity (raf' al-hadath) or to perform salah, or simply intending wudu or obeying Allah's command. The place is the heart; verbal utterance is recommended by the mashayikh. The reason niyyah is only sunnah (mahmudah) in wudu is that the Quranic command only requires washing and wiping (no mention of intention), and the Prophet did not teach it to the bedouin (who did not know). However, niyyah is fard in tayammum because tayammum uses earth, which is not intrinsically purifying, so intention distinguishes it from mere dust.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): Resolve of the heart to perform an action for worship
الاستنجاء (al-istinja'): Cleansing after using the toilet

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is intention considered sunnah in wudu but fard in tayammum according to the Hashiya?
A) Because wudu is more important
B) Because tayammum uses earth, which is not inherently purifying, so intention is needed
C) Because the Prophet never did wudu with intention
D) Because tayammum is a substitute

Key Takeaway
Intention in wudu is sunnah, not fard; its fard status in tayammum highlights the role of intention when the purifying agent is not intrinsically purifying.

Tarteeb in Wudu: Sunnah Not Fard
Ruling on order of washing limbs in wudu and its proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that tarteeb (order) in wudu is sunnah muakkadah, not fard, and identify the linguistic evidence from the Quranic verse.

Core Idea
The waw in the verse indicates conjunction, not order, so tarteeb is sunnah, not fard.

Many assume that the order of washing limbs in wudu is obligatory because the Quran lists them in a specific sequence. However, the Hanafi school holds that order is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah), not a requirement for validity. This lesson unpacks the linguistic reasoning behind this position, focusing on the function of the Arabic conjunctions 'waw' and 'fa' in the verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and state the Hanafi ruling on tarteeb in wudu. Notice the phrase 'sunnah muakkadah' and the negation of fard.
The ruling is explicit: it is a confirmed sunnah, not obligatory.
2
Analyze the linguistic evidence
The passage argues that the 'waw' (واو) in the verse is for absolute conjunction, not sequential order. The 'fa' in 'fāghsilū' indicates immediate sequence of the entire washing act, not internal order among the limbs. Understand the distinction between the two conjunctions.
The analogy of 'enter the market and buy bread and meat' clarifies the point.
3
Evaluate the opposing view
Consider the Shafi'i position that tarteeb is fard. They interpret the 'fa' as imposing sequential order among the limbs. Contrast this with the Hanafi interpretation.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that washing feet before face invalidates wudu in the Shafi'i school but not in the Hanafi.
4
Note the incomplete evidence
The passage begins to cite a hadith (the bedouin hadith) but is cut off. Recognize that the complete dalil includes both Quranic linguistic analysis and prophetic practice, but the linguistic argument is the primary proof here.
The missing hadith is well-known in other sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسن الترتيب سنة مؤكدة في الصحيح كما نص الله تعالى في كتابه ولم يكن فرضاً لأن الواو في الأمر لمطلق الجمع والفاء التي في قوله تعالى فاغسلوا للتعقيب جملة الأعضاء من غير إفادة طلب تقديم بعضها على بعض في الوجود، فهو كقولك : ادخل السوق فاشتر لنا خبزاً ولحماً حيث كان المفاد إعقاب الدخول بشراء ما ذكر، والدليل لنا ما رواه
And it is Sunnah, a confirmed Sunnah in the correct view, as Allah the Most High has stated in His book, but it is not fard because the waw in the command is for absolute conjunction, and the fa in His statement 'So wash' is for immediate sequence of the limbs collectively, without indicating a requirement of prioritizing some over others in existence. So it is like your saying: 'Enter the market and buy for us bread and meat' where the meaning is the sequence of entering with buying what was mentioned. And the evidence for us is what was narrated...
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This is a ruling on tarteeb (order) in wudu, stating that it is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) but not fard. The Hashiya explains the reasoning: The Quranic verse uses the letter 'waw' (wa) which indicates conjunction without order, and the 'fa' (fā) in 'fāghsilū' indicates sequence of the entire limbs together, not sequential order. The analogy given is if one says 'Enter the market and buy bread and meat' - the 'fa' implies entering then buying, but doesn't specify which item to buy first. Similarly, the Quran commands washing face, hands, etc. with 'fa' showing the general sequence from the beginning to the end, but not requiring internal order among the limbs. The text begins to mention a hadith as evidence (the bedouin hadith) but is cut off.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tarteeb): Order of washing the limbs in wudu as mentioned in the Quran (face, hands, head, feet).
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah muakkadah): Confirmed Sunnah; an act the Prophet consistently performed and emphasized but not obligatory.
الواو (al-waw): The Arabic conjunction 'and', which in Hanafi usul indicates absolute conjunction without sequential order.
الفاء (al-fa): The Arabic particle indicating immediate succession; in this context, it links the washing command to the preceding context and indicates the overall sequence of the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hashiya, why is tarteeb (order) not fard in wudu?
A) Because the verse uses 'waw' which implies order
B) Because the 'fa' in 'fāghsilū' indicates sequence of the entire washing, not internal limb order
C) Because the Prophet did not follow order
D) Because order is impossible to maintain

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, tarteeb in wudu is a confirmed sunnah, not a fard, because the Quranic conjunctives do not impose a specific order among the limbs.

intermediate
6 min
The Ruling of Niyyah in Wudu: Sunnah, Not Fard
Defines niyyah and establishes it as sunnah in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on niyyah in wudu, explain the evidence from the Quran and Prophetic practice, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Intention in wudu is sunnah, not fard—because the Quran and Prophet did not command it.

This lesson clarifies the legal status of intention (niyyah) in wudu according to the Hanafi school. More than just a rule, it reveals a major usul principle: rulings are derived from explicit commands and prophetic practice. We will examine the definition, timing, and the key proofs that set the Hanafi view apart from others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Niyyah in wudu is ruled sunnah (or mustahabb per al-Quduri). Not fard, not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is from the Qur'an (5:6) and the Prophet's teaching to the Bedouin. The verse commands washing and wiping but does not mention intention.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The absence of an explicit command for intention in the verse indicates it is not obligatory. Similarly, the Prophet did not instruct the Bedouin about intention, despite his ignorance, showing it is not essential for validity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds niyyah as fard in wudu. Even within Hanafi, al-Quduri considers it mustahabb. The difference arises from how they interpret the command in the verse.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi reliance on the apparent meaning of the Qur'an and the sunnah supports that intention is not obligatory. The mufta bihi is that it is sunnah, as stated by the mashayikh.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة (النية) وهي لغة عزم القلب على الفعل واصطلاحاً توجه القلب لايجاد الفعل جزماً، ووقتها قبل الاستنجاء ليكون جميع فعله قربة وكيفيتها أن ينوي رفع الحدث أو إقامة الصلاة أو ينوي الوضوء، أو امتثال الأمر ومحلها القلب فإن نطق بها ليجمع بين فعل القلب، واللسان استحبه المشايخ والنية سنة لتحصيل الثواب لأنّ المأمور به ليس إلا غسلاً، ومسحا في الآية ولم يعلمه النبي لا للإعرابي مع جهله وفرضت في التيمم لأنه بالتراب وليس مزيلاً للحدث بالأصالة قوله : (وهي لغة خلط الفعل كذا قاله الجوهري، وهو . إصطلاح بآخر كما هو . دأبه لأنه معناها الشرعي، وأما معناها لغة فليس في كلام أهل اللغة إلا أنها من نوى الشيء قصده وتوجه إليه، والشارح عكس المعنيين. قوله : (لايجاد الفعل جزماً الفعل أعم من فعل المأمورات وترك المنهيات، ومدار الأمرين عليها لأن المكلف به في النهي هو كف النفس على الراجح لكن اعتبار النية للمتروك إنما هو الحصول الثواب لا للخروج عن عهدة النهي فإن مجرد الترك فيه كاف، فلا يستحق الوعيد. قوله : (أو ينوي الوضوء ولو نوى الطهارة يكفيه عن البعض إعتباراً له بالتيمم قاله الزيلعي . قوله: (استحبه المشايخ) فالمراد أنهم استحسنوه لجمعه مع القلب ولم يرد التلفظ بها عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا عن الصحابة والتابعين، والأئمة رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين. قوله : (والنية سنة) وقال القدوري : إنها مستحبة قوله : (لأن المأمور به ليس إلا غسلاً ومسحاً) ربما تفيد هذه العبارة أن الوضوء المأمور به لا تشترط له النية قال الحموي والتحقيق أن الوضوء المأمور به يتأدى بغير نية لأن المأمور به حصوله لا تحصيله كسائر الشروط وفي الإشباه عن بعض الكتب الوضوء الذي ليس بمنوي ليس بمأمور به ولكنه مفتاح للصلاة اهـ فإن أريد بالمأمور به ما يثاب عليه إرتفع التنافي قوله: (ولم يعمله النبي ( الواو حالية والظاهر تأنيثه لرجوعه إلى النية . قوله: (لأنه بالتراب) أي وهو لم يعتبر مطهراً شرعاً إلا للصلاة وتوابعها لا في نفسه فكان التطهير به تعبداً محضاً، وفيه يحتاج إلى النية كما في الفتح أو لأن لفظه ينبيء عن القصد، والأصل أن يعتبر في الأسماء الشرعية ما تنبىء عنه من المعاني .
Book of Purification (Intention) It is linguistically: determination of the heart to do an action. Technically: the heart's direction to create the action definitively. Its time is before istinja so that all his action becomes worship. Its manner is that he intends removal of hadath, or performing prayer, or he intends wudu, or obeying the command. Its place is the heart; if he utters it to combine the action of the heart and tongue, the mashayikh considered it commendable. Intention is sunnah to attain reward, because the commanded action is only washing and wiping in the verse, and the Prophet did not teach it to the Bedouin despite his ignorance. It is made fard in tayammum because it is with earth and it is not essentially a remover of hadath. His saying: (It is linguistically mixing the action - thus said al-Jawhari, and it is another terminology as is his custom because it is its legal meaning, but its linguistic meaning is not in the speech of the linguists except that it is from 'nawa al-shay'a' meaning he intended and aimed at it, and the commentator reversed the two meanings. His saying: (To create the action definitively) The action is general including commanded acts and leaving prohibited acts, and the two matters revolve around it because what the mukallaf is charged with in prohibitions is refraining the soul according to the rajih, but considering intention for what is left is only to obtain reward, not to exit the obligation of the prohibition, because mere leaving is sufficient in it, so he does not deserve punishment. His saying: (Or he intends wudu) If he intends purification it suffices him according to some, considering it analogically to tayammum, al-Zayla'i said it. His saying: (The mashayikh considered it commendable) Meaning they considered it good because it combines with the heart, and uttering intention has not been reported from the Prophet nor from the Sahaba and Tabi'in and Imams, may Allah be pleased with them all. His saying: (And intention is sunnah) Al-Quduri said it is mustahabb. His saying: (Because the commanded action is only washing and wiping) This statement might imply that the commanded wudu does not require intention. Al-Hamawi said: The verification is that commanded wudu is performed without intention because what is commanded is its occurrence not its acquisition like other conditions. In al-Ishbah from some books: wudu that is not intended is not commanded but it is a key for prayer. If by commanded is meant that which is rewarded, then the contradiction is resolved. His saying: (And he did not teach it to the Prophet) The waw is halal and the apparent is its feminization because it refers to intention. His saying: (Because it is with earth) i.e., it is not considered a purifier legally except for prayer and its accompaniments, not in itself, so purification by it is pure worship, and it needs intention as in al-Fath, or because its word indicates intention, and the principle is that in legal names what they indicate of meanings is considered.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage defines the legal term 'niyyah' (intention) and addresses its ruling in wudu. The author begins by giving the linguistic and technical definitions. Linguistically, it is the heart's determination; technically, it is the heart's direction to perform an action with certainty. The time for intention is before istinja' (cleaning oneself) so that all actions become acts of worship. The manner of intending is to intend either removal of ritual impurity (hadath), or performing prayer, or wudu itself, or obeying Allah's command. Its place is the heart; uttering it verbally is commendable according to later scholars (mashayikh) as it combines heart and tongue. The ruling is that intention is sunnah (or mustahabb according to al-Quduri), not fard, because the Quranic verse (5:6) only commands washing and wiping, and the Prophet did not teach intention to the Bedouin who came asking about wudu. The exception is tayammum, where intention is fard because tayammum is a purely devotional act not essentially removing impurity. The commentary refines the definitions, explains that intention is not required for the validity of wudu but for reward, and discusses the linguistic nuances. The Hanafi position is clear: niyyah in wudu is sunnah, not fard, supported by the absence of any explicit command and by the practice of the Prophet.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): The heart's direction to create an action definitively (tawajjuh al-qalb li-ijad al-fi'l jazman)
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): Cleaning the private parts after relieving oneself

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this text, what is the ruling of niyyah in wudu?
A) Fard
B) Sunnah
C) Wajib
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that intention in wudu is a sunnah for reward, not a fard or condition of validity, based on the absence of explicit command in the Quran and the Prophet's practice.

Sunnah Practices of Wudu: Order and Starting Preferences
Lists and proves multiple sunnah acts in wudu with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five sunnah acts of wudu mentioned in the text, identify the Hanafi proof that order (tarteeb) is sunnah not fard, and distinguish the mufta bihi position from weaker opinions.

Core Idea
Order in wudu is sunnah, not fard — the Quranic waw combines, and the tayammum hadith proves it.

Wudu is a foundational act of worship with many recommended practices that perfect it. This passage from Maraqi al-Falah and its commentary clarifies several sunnah acts — from the sequence of washing to which side to start with — and provides the textual and rational proofs for each. You will learn not only the rulings but also the legal reasoning that distinguishes a sunnah from a fard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five sunnah acts
Read the source text and list the five specific sunnah acts mentioned: order (tarteeb), beginning with the right (al-bida'ah bil-mayamin), washing from the fingertips, wiping from the front of the head, and wiping the neck.
Also note what is explicitly excluded: wiping the throat is bid'ah.
2
Analyze the evidence for tarteeb
Focus on the argument that order is sunnah, not fard. Identify the two key proofs: (1) The Quranic waw indicates mere combination, not sequence. (2) The hadith of tayammum where the Prophet began with his forearms before his face — showing order is not required in wudu either.
Understand the analogy (qiyas) between wudu and tayammum in this regard.
3
Examine the proof for beginning with the right
The hadith 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right sides' is cited. Note how the imperative is turned from obligation to recommendation by consensus (ijma') due to the honor of the right.
The scope is limited to paired limbs (hands, feet); the face and single limbs are excluded.
4
Understand the ikhtilaf on the last four acts
Some scholars consider the last four acts (from mayamin onward) as merely mustahabb, not sunnah mu'akkadah. The text rejects this by affirming that constancy (muwazabah) is established.
The author sides with the stronger view and states that doing them is better than leaving them.
5
Apply the rulings to a practical scenario
Consider a person who washes his feet before his hands in wudu. Using the Hanafi position, determine that wudu is valid but the sunnah of order is missed. Contrast with the Shafi'i view that order is fard, which would invalidate the wudu.
This thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is the key takeaway.

وبــــــه بــــديــــنــــا ولــو عــبــدنـا غـیـره شقينا من أبي وقيل : إنه أنشد ذلك كما هو عند الحرث بن أسامة من طريق سليمان التيمي عن عثمان. قوله : (في اليدين والرجلين وهما عضوان مغسولان فخرج العضو الواحد كالوجه فلا يطلب فيه التيامن والعضوان الممسوحان كالأذنين ،والخفين فالسنة مسحهما معاً لكونه أسهل قال في السراج : إلا إذا كان أقطع فإنه يبدأ بالأيمن منها يعني من الخدين، والأذنين، والخفين قوله : وهي أوضح وأولى. قوله : (البداءة في الماء المسح وأما البداءة في الغسل بصب أعلى سطح الجبهة فقال ابن أمير حاج أنه أدب. قوله : (من مقدم الرأس لما تقدم في الحديث قوله : (لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم الخ ) مثله في الشرح، والسيد، وغيرهما، وهو يقتضي ان الرقبة مع مسح الرأس عند ذهاب اليدين إلى مؤخر الرأس، وهو خلاف المتداول بين الناس، وما في الفتح من أنه يستحب مسح الرقبة بظهر اليدين لعدم استعمال بلتهما فموهم لأن مفهومه إن بلة باطنهما مستعملة، وليس كذلك أفاده الحموي وروي عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أنه كان إذا توضأ مسح عنقه، ويقول : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «من عنقه لم يغل بالأغلال يوم القيامة». قوله : (وليس مسلماً) أي بل المواظبة ثابتة قال في الشرح : وعند اختلاف الأقوال كان فعله أولى من تركه ،اهـ وفيه أنه لم يقل أحد بتركه وإنما الخلاف في تأكده واستحبابه فكان الأولى حذفها.
(And) order (tarteeb) is sunnah, strongly confirmed according to the correct view, and it is (as Allah the Exalted has stated in His Book). It is not fard because the waw in the command is for absolute combination, and the fa in His saying 'fa-ghsilu' indicates... His saying: (And it is) as Allah the Exalted has stated in His Book, the verse is devoid of indication of that; rather the specification comes from his action, peace be upon him. His saying: 'Continuity of all the limbs without requesting the precedence of some over others in existence, so it is like your saying: Enter the market and buy for us bread and meat, where the benefit is the continuation of entry with the purchase of what is mentioned. The evidence for us is what was reported for continuity of all the limbs. (And) it is sunnah (beginning with the right sides, plural of maimanah, opposite of maisarah, in the hands and feet) because of his saying: 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right sides,' and the command is turned from obligation by consensus to its desirability due to the honor of the right. (And) it is sunnah to begin washing from (the tips of the fingers) in the hands and feet, because Allah the Exalted made the elbows and ankles the limit of washing, so they are the end of the action, as the Prophet, peace be upon him, did. (And) it is sunnah to begin wiping from (the front of the head). And (wiping the neck) is sunnah because he, peace be upon him, performed wudu and gestured with his hands from the front of his head until he reached the bottom of his neck from the nape. And (wiping the throat) is not sunnah; rather it is an innovation. It was said that the last four, the first of which is beginning with the right, are (mustahabb), and it seems that its aspect is the lack of established constancy, but it is not accepted. Al-Bukhari and Abu Dawud reported that he performed tayammum and began with his forearms before his face. Since the absence of order in tayammum is established, it is established in wudu because the ruling on both is the same. By this, you know the fall of the saying of whoever said: It should be wajib due to constancy... etc. His saying: (And beginning with the right sides is sunnah) The word 'al-bida'ah' has three pronunciations, and it is the language of the Ansar. Ibn Rawaha said: 'We began with the name of Allah and we have started with Him, if we worshipped other than Him we would be wretched.' It was said that he recited that as it is in the narration of al-Harith ibn Usama. His saying: (In the hands and feet they are two washed limbs, so the single limb like the face is excluded, so tayammun is not required for it, and the two wiped limbs like the ears and the khuffs, so the sunnah is to wipe them together because it is easier. In al-Siraj: except if he is amputated, then he begins with the right of them, meaning of the cheeks, ears, and khuffs. His saying: 'So it will be the end of the action,' i.e., the end necessarily has a beginning in the limb, and washing all of it is prescribed, so the beginning is its first part. His saying: (As the Prophet did) i.e., the mentioned beginning, and the kaf is for cause, and his expression in the sharh: 'And because the Prophet used to do this' is clearer and better. His saying: (The beginning in water is wiping, and as for the beginning in washing by pouring on the top of the forehead, Ibn Amir Hajj said it is good manners. His saying: (From the front of the head) based on what preceded in the hadith. His saying: (Because he, peace be upon him, etc.) similar in the sharh, al-Sayyid, and others. It implies that the neck is with wiping the head when the hands go to the back of the head, which is contrary to common practice among people. What is in al-Fath that it is recommended to wipe the neck with the backs of the hands because their moisture is not used is mistaken because its implication is that the moisture of the palms is used, and it is not so, as al-Hamawi stated. It was narrated from Ibn Umar that when he performed wudu he wiped his neck and said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever wipes his neck will not be shackled with chains on the Day of Resurrection.' His saying: (And it is not accepted) i.e., rather constancy is established. In al-Sharh: When there is difference of opinions, doing it is better than leaving it. In it, no one said to leave it; rather the difference is about its being strongly confirmed and recommended, so it would have been better to omit it.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling on tarteeb (order) in wudu: it is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard, because the Quranic conjunction 'waw' indicates mere combination, not sequence, and the 'fa' in 'fa-ghsilu' does not demand order. The proof is the hadith of tayammum where the Prophet started with his forearms before his face, showing that order is not required in tayammum, and by analogy, in wudu. Then it lists several sunnah acts: beginning with the right side (mayaamin) in washing the hands and feet, based on the hadith 'Begin with your right sides,' which is turned from obligation to recommendation by consensus due to the honor of the right side. Next, it is sunnah to begin washing from the fingertips (ru'us al-asabi') because the elbows are the limit, so the end implies a beginning. Similarly, beginning wiping from the front of the head (muqaddam al-ra's) is sunnah. Wiping the neck (mash al-raqabah) is also sunnah according to the report of Ibn Umar and the practice of the Prophet, though some consider it mustahabb. Wiping the throat (halqum) is not sunnah and is considered an innovation. The commentary provides linguistic notes on 'al-bida'ah', discusses the scope of mayaamin (applicable only to pairs of limbs, not the face or single limbs), and addresses the method of wiping the neck (with the backs of the hands or with water). The author concludes that the relied-upon view is that these acts are sunnah, and the objection about lack of constancy is not accepted.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tarteeb): Continuity of the limbs (ta'qib jumlat al-a'da') i.e., washing them in sequence without unnecessary delay
البداءة بالميامن (al-bida'ah bil-mayamin): Beginning with the right side in washing paired limbs (hands, feet)
مسح الرقبة (mash al-raqabah): Wiping the neck during wudu

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence used in the text to prove that order (tarteeb) is not fard in wudu?
A) An explicit Quranic verse
B) The hadith of tayammum where the Prophet began with forearms before face
C) Consensus of the Salaf
D) The hadith 'Begin with your right sides'

Key Takeaway
Order (tarteeb) and other preferences in wudu are sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard; omitting them does not invalidate wudu but loses reward.

The Sunnah of Starting with the Right Side in Wudu
Ruling on beginning wudu with the right side, with proof and scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on starting wudu with the right side and identify the limbs to which it applies.

Core Idea
Starting wudu with the right side is sunnah, not wajib, and applies only to paired washed limbs.

In this lesson, we examine a key sunnah act of wudu: beginning with the right side. The text clarifies that this is a recommended practice, not an obligation, despite the imperative form of the hadith. We will explore the proof, the reasoning behind the sunnah classification, and the precise scope of which limbs are included.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is beginning wudu with the right side (tayammun). The Hanafi ruling is that it is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is the hadith: 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right sides.' This is a command from the Prophet.
The hadith is ahad, so its transmission is zanni.
3
Analyze the legal interpretation
The imperative form normally indicates obligation, but the Hanafis divert it to recommendation due to consensus (ijma) that it is not obligatory, and the honor of the right side.
The consensus is the key factor that overrides the default implication of the command.
4
Define the scope
The sunnah applies only to paired washed limbs: hands and feet. It does not apply to single limbs (face) or wiped limbs (ears, khuffs). An exception is made for an amputee, who begins with the right of the remaining parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لتعقيب جملة الأعضاء (و) يسن (البداءة بالميامن جمع ميمنة خلاف الميسرة في اليدين والرجلين لقوله : إذا توضأتم فابدؤا بميامنكم، وصرف الأمر عن الوجوب بالإجماع على استحبابه لشرف اليمنى . قوله: (ويسن) البداءة بالميامن البداءة بتثليث الباء، والمد والهمز وتبدل ياء، وهي لغة الأنصار قال ابن رواحة : باس الإله وبـــــه بــــديــــنــــا ولــو عــبــدنـا غـیـره شقينا من أبي وقيل : إنه أنشد ذلك كما هو عند الحرث بن أسامة من طريق سليمان التيمي عن عثمان. قوله: (في اليدين والرجلين وهما عضوان مغسولان فخرج العضو الواحد كالوجه فلا يطلب فيه التيامن والعضوان الممسوحان كالأذنين ،والخفين فالسنة مسحهما معاً لكونه أسهل قال في السراج : إلا إذا كان أقطع فإنه يبدأ بالأيمن منها يعني من الخدين، والأذنين، والخفين
For the order of the limbs, and it is sunnah to begin with the right sides, plural of maymanah as opposed to maysarah, in the hands and feet, because of his statement: 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right sides.' And the command is diverted from obligation by consensus to it being recommended due to the honor of the right side. His statement: 'And it is sunnah' – beginning with the right sides: 'al-bada'ah' with three possible vowel patterns for the ba, and with lengthening and hamz, or with ya substituted, and it is the dialect of the Ansar. Ibn Rawaha said: 'Bismillah we began...' [verse]. His statement: 'In the hands and feet' – they are two washed limbs, so the single limb like the face is excluded, thus tayammun is not required for it, and the two wiped limbs like the ears and khuffs, so the sunnah is to wipe them both together because it is easier. Al-Siraj said: Except if he is amputated, then he begins with the right of them, meaning from the cheeks, ears, and khuffs.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hashiya on the sunnah of beginning wudu with the right side. The author first quotes the matn stating that it is sunnah to start with the right side (al-maymanah) for the hands and feet, based on the hadith 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right sides.' He clarifies that the command is not for obligation (wujub) but for recommendation (istihbab) by consensus (ijma), due to the honor of the right side. The commentator then provides a linguistic note on the word 'al-bada'ah' (beginning) and quotes a verse from Ibn Rawaha. He further explains that this sunnah applies only to paired washed limbs (hands and feet), not to single limbs like the face, nor to wiped limbs like the ears and khuffs; for those, the sunnah is to wipe both together. An exception is made for an amputee, who should begin with the right of the remaining parts (cheeks, ears, or khuffs). The overall authority is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as the ruling is standard in the school.

Key Terms
البداءة (al-bada'ah): The act of beginning or starting, with variant pronunciations.
الميامن (al-mayamin): Right sides, plural of maymanah, meaning the right hand and foot.
التيامن (al-tayammun): The act of starting with the right side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) All limbs including the face
B) Only the hands and feet (paired washed limbs)
C) Only the ears and khuffs (wiped limbs)
D) Only the face

Key Takeaway
Starting wudu with the right side is a sunnah for paired washed limbs, based on a hadith whose imperative is interpreted as recommendation due to consensus.

The Sunnah of Starting Washing from the Fingertips
Ruling on beginning the wash from the fingertips based on the end-point of the limbs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah of beginning wudu from the fingertips and identify the Quranic and Prophetic proofs for it.

Core Idea
The endpoint implies a start: washing begins at the fingertips because the limbs extend to the elbows and ankles.

In this lesson, we examine a specific sunnah act in wudu: starting the washing of the hands and feet from the fingertips. The Hanafi school derives this from the Quranic specification of the washing limits (elbows and ankles) and the practice of the Prophet. Understanding this ruling helps you perform wudu with fuller adherence to the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
State the sunnah ruling
Identify what the matn says: it is sunnah to begin washing from the tips of the fingers and toes.
Not obligatory, but recommended.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
Locate the ayat of wudu (5:6) and note the words 'to the elbows' and 'to the ankles'. The commentator argues that these endpoints imply a beginning, which is the opposite side.
3
Connect to the Prophetic practice
The text states that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to start from the fingertips, providing the sunnah example.
The kaf in 'kama' indicates causation.
4
Distinguish from the forehead
Note the clarification: starting by pouring water on the top of the forehead is merely adab, not sunnah, as stated by Ibn Amir Haj.
This shows precision in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن البداءة بالغسل من (رؤس الأصابع) في اليدين، والرجلين لأن الله تعالى جعل المرافق والكعبين غاية الغسل فتكون منتهى الفعل كما فعله النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قوله: فتكون منتهى (الفعل) أي والمنتهى لا بد له من مبدا في العضو، وقد فرض غسل جميعه، فالمبدأ أوله قوله : (كما فعله النبي ) أي البداءة المذكورة، والكاف للعلة، وعبارته في الشرح ولأن النبي ما كان يفعل هكذا اهـ وهي أوضح وأولى. قوله : (البداءة في الماء المسح وأما البداءة في الغسل بصب أعلى سطح الجبهة فقال ابن أمير حاج أنه أدب.
And it is sunnah to begin washing from the tips of the fingers in the hands and feet, because Allah Almighty made the elbows and ankles the end-point of washing, so it becomes the end of the action, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did. His statement: 'so it becomes the end of the action' – meaning that the endpoint must have a beginning in the limb, and washing the entire limb is obligatory, so the beginning is its first part. His statement: 'as the Prophet did' – meaning the mentioned beginning, and the kaf is for reason. The expression in the Sharh is 'because the Prophet used to do it thus' which is clearer and better. His statement: 'the beginning in water for wiping, but the beginning in washing by pouring on the upper part of the forehead – Ibn Amir Haj said it is adab.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hashiya on the sunnah of starting the washing of the hands and feet from the fingertips. The matn states that it is sunnah to begin from the fingertips of the hands and feet because Allah made the elbows and ankles the end-point (ghayah) of washing, so the endpoint necessitates a starting point, which is the fingertips. The commentator explains that since the entire limb must be washed, the natural beginning is the tip, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did. He also notes that the word 'as' in 'as the Prophet did' indicates the reason, and the Sharh version is clearer. He then distinguishes between beginning in washing (ghusl) and wiping (mash), stating that beginning by pouring water on the top of the forehead is adab, not sunnah. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is well-established in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
رؤس الأصابع (ru'us al-asabi'): The tips of the fingers and toes.
المرافق والكعبين (al-marafiq wa al-ka'bayn): The elbows and ankles, the end-points of washing in wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Starting wudu from the fingertips is a confirmed sunnah of the Prophet, derived from the Quran's specification of the washing limits.

Sunnah Acts in Wiping the Head and Neck
Rulings on wiping the head from the front, the neck, and prohibition of wiping the throat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the sunnah acts of wiping the head and neck, and identify the innovation of wiping the throat.

Core Idea
Wiping the neck is sunnah; wiping the throat is bid'ah. Start from the front of the head.

In performing wudu, the sequence and method of wiping the head are guided by the Prophet's practice. While the obligatory act is wiping a portion of the head, the sunnah adds specific details. This passage clarifies which acts are recommended and which are innovations, ensuring our worship follows the pure sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
The matn states three distinct rulings: (1) It is sunnah to begin wiping from the front of the head. (2) It is sunnah to wipe the neck. (3) It is not sunnah to wipe the throat; rather it is an innovation.
These are laid out as separate legal statements.
2
Note the proofs for each ruling
The proofs cited: For the front of the head, it is based on the general hadith about wiping the head. For the neck, the Prophet's action (gesturing from front to back including neck) and the hadith from Ibn Umar promising reward. For the throat, there is no proof; it is rejected as innovation.
The hadith 'Whoever wipes his neck...' indicates reward, implying recommendation.
3
Understand the commentary on the method
The commentator clarifies that the neck is wiped as part of the head wipe when hands reach the back, not separately. He refutes the view that the back of the hands should be used, stating the inner palms' moisture is not used.
This harmonizes practice with the Prophetic example.
4
Recognize the bid'ah ruling
The text explicitly says wiping the throat (halqum) is not sunnah but innovation. There is no basis in the sunnah for this act.
Bid'ah means an innovation in religion, which is prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن البداءة في المسح من (مقدم الرأس و يسن (مسح الرقبة) لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم توضاً وأوما بيديه من مقدم رأسه حتى بلغ بهما أسفل عنقه من قبل قفاه و(لا) يسن مسح (الحلقوم) بل هو بدعة قوله: (من مقدم الرأس) لما تقدم في الحديث قوله: (لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم الخ ) مثله في الشرح، والسيد، وغيرهما، وهو يقتضي ان الرقبة مع مسح الرأس عند ذهاب اليدين إلى مؤخر الرأس، وهو خلاف المتداول بين الناس، وما في الفتح من أنه يستحب مسح الرقبة بظهر اليدين لعدم استعمال بلتهما فموهم لأن مفهومه إن بلة باطنهما مستعملة، وليس كذلك أفاده الحموي وروي عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أنه كان إذا توضأ مسح عنقه، ويقول : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «من عنقه لم يغل بالأغلال يوم القيامة».
And it is sunnah to begin wiping from the front of the head, and it is sunnah to wipe the neck, because he (peace be upon him) performed wudu and gestured with his hands from the front of his head until they reached the lower part of his neck from the back. And it is not sunnah to wipe the throat; rather it is an innovation. His statement: 'from the front of the head' due to what preceded in the hadith. His statement: 'because he...' etc. similar in the Sharh, and al-Sayyid, etc., and it implies that the neck is included with the wiping of the head when the hands go to the back of the head, contrary to common practice. What is in al-Fath that it is recommended to wipe the neck with the back of the hands because their moisture is not used is misleading, because its implication is that the moisture of the inner palms is used, which is not the case, as al-Hamawi clarified. And it is narrated from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) that when he performed wudu, he wiped his neck and said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever wipes his neck will not be shackled with chains on the Day of Resurrection.'
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings with proofs from the Hashiya on the sunnah of wiping the head and neck, and the prohibition of wiping the throat. The matn states three things: (1) It is sunnah to begin wiping from the front of the head. (2) It is sunnah to wipe the neck. (3) It is not sunnah to wipe the throat (halqum); rather it is bid'ah (innovation). The commentator explains that wiping the neck is sunnah based on the Prophet's action and the hadith from Ibn Umar. He notes that the neck is wiped as part of wiping the head when the hands move to the back, contrary to the common practice of wiping the neck separately. He also criticizes the view in al-Fath that one should wipe the neck with the back of the hands, arguing that the inner palms are not used (and thus their moisture is not 'used' in the sense of being consumed), so the back of the hands is not necessary. The hadith about wiping the neck removing chains is cited as encouragement. The ruling that wiping the throat is bid'ah is clear: it is not part of the sunnah. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah, with the hadith from Ibn Umar supporting the sunnah of neck wiping.

Key Terms
مقدم الرأس (muqaddam al-ra's): The front part of the head where wiping begins.
مسح الرقبة (mash al-raqabah): Wiping the neck, considered sunnah in Hanafi wudu.
الحلقوم (al-halqum): The throat or windpipe; wiping it is bid'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wiping the neck
B) Wiping the head from the front
C) Wiping the throat
D) Wiping the ears

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wudu, it is sunnah to begin wiping the head from the front and to wipe the neck; wiping the throat is an innovation.

Are These Sunan Mustahab or Sunnah Mu'akkadah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute over the status of four wudu acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the majority Hanafi position considers the four acts (starting with right, from fingertips, wiping front of head, wiping neck) as sunnah mu'akkadah and evaluate the argument of those who consider them mustahab.

Core Idea
The Prophet's consistency (muwazabah) elevates an act from mustahab to sunnah mu'akkadah.

In wudu, there are four actions whose legal status is debated within the Hanafi school: starting with the right side, starting from the fingertips, wiping the front of the head, and wiping the neck. Some scholars classify them as mustahab (recommended), while the majority hold them to be sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). This lesson examines the basis of the disagreement and the evidence that settles it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed acts and the two positions
List the four acts: starting with the right, starting from fingertips, wiping front of head, wiping neck. One view says they are mustahab; the other says sunnah mu'akkadah.
The dispute is not about whether to do them, but about the degree of emphasis.
2
Understand the criterion of muwazabah
Muwazabah means the Prophet's consistent practice without significant omission. In Hanafi usul, consistency is key to distinguishing sunnah mu'akkadah from mustahab.
3
Analyze the argument for mustahab
Proponents of mustahab claim that the Prophet's consistency (muwazabah) is not firmly established for these acts, so they are less emphasized.
4
Examine the rebuttal that muwazabah is established
The commentator rejects the claim, stating that muwazabah is indeed proven. He quotes al-Sharh that when opinions differ, doing the act is better than leaving it.
The disagreement is only about emphasis, not about abandoning the act.
5
Conclude the relied-upon position
The mufta bihi is that these acts are sunnah mu'akkadah. The designation 'mustahab' is better omitted because no one advocates leaving them entirely.
Authority weight: later Hanafi scholarship (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل أن الأربعة الأخيرة التي أوّلها البداءة بالميامن (مستحبة) وكأن وجهه عدم ثبوت المواظبة وليس مسلماً . قوله : (وليس مسلماً) أي بل المواظبة ثابتة قال في الشرح : وعند اختلاف الأقوال كان فعله أولى من تركه ،اهـ وفيه أنه لم يقل أحد بتركه وإنما الخلاف في تأكده واستحبابه فكان الأولى حذفها.
And it is said that the last four, the first of which is starting with the right side, are mustahab (recommended), as if its reason is the lack of established consistency, but it is not accepted. His statement: 'and it is not accepted' – meaning rather the consistency is established. He said in al-Sharh: When opinions differ, doing it is better than leaving it. But it contains that no one said to leave it; the disagreement is only about its emphasis and recommendation, so it would be better to omit it.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the status of the four sunnah acts (starting with the right side, starting from fingertips, wiping from front of head, wiping the neck). Some scholars consider them mustahab (recommended) rather than sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), claiming that the Prophet did not consistently perform them. However, the commentator rejects this view, stating that consistency (muwazabah) is indeed established. He quotes al-Sharh that when opinions differ, performing the act is better than leaving it. He notes that no one advocates leaving these acts entirely; the disagreement is only over the degree of emphasis. Therefore, it would be better to omit the designation 'mustahab' and simply keep them as sunnah. The authority weight is from the later Hanafi scholarship (fatawa mutakhkhirin), as the Zahir al-Riwayah does not explicitly differentiate between sunnah and mustahab for these acts. The mufta bihi is that they are sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms
مستحبة (mustahabbah): Recommended but not emphasized; lower than sunnah mu'akkadah.
المواظبة (al-muwazabah): Consistency or regularity of the Prophet's practice.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): Emphasized sunnah; leaving it without excuse is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Mustahab (recommended)
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Wajib (obligatory)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the four acts are sunnah mu'akkadah because the Prophet's consistency (muwazabah) is established; the minority mustahab view is not acted upon.

Definition and Etiquettes of Wudu: Distinguishing Adab from Sunnah
Definition and list of etiquettes (adab) of wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define adab, distinguish it from sunnah based on consistency and consequence, and list the fourteen etiquettes of wudu.

Core Idea
Adab are recommended acts with reward but no blame; sunnah carries reproach for intentional omission.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi introduces the concept of adab in wudu, clarifying its legal status as a category distinct from sunnah. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly evaluating the reward and blame associated with various prophetic practices.

Guided Path
1
Define adab
The text defines adab both linguistically ('putting things in their places') and technically ('what the Prophet did once or twice without consistency').
Multiple definitions given; they are close.
2
Distinguish adab from sunnah
Sunnah is consistent practice; leaving it brings reproach. Adab is inconsistent; leaving it has no blame.
Both bring reward.
3
List the fourteen adab
The text enumerates fourteen items: sitting elevated, facing qiblah except during istinja, vessel placement, not seeking help, no worldly talk, combining heart and tongue intention, transmitted supplications, tasmiyah, etc.
Some sources expand to over sixty.
4
Note the commentary on specific adab
Commentary clarifies that 'not seeking help' is not disliked, and verbalizing intention (al-'azimah) means strengthening resolve, not a legal requirement.
Derived from hadith and practice of Companions.
5
Apply the ruling
Following adab is recommended (mandub/mustahab). Omitting them does not invalidate wudu but loses reward.
Contrast with sunnah mu'akkadah which carries reproach for leaving.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أكرم المجالس ما استقبل به القبلة. قوله: (وعدم الإستعانة بغيره) قال الكرماني : لا كراهة في الصب، ولا يقال إنّه خلاف الأولى، وساق عدة أحاديث دالة على أن النبي ،فعله، وضعف ما يدل على الكراهة، وممن كان يستعين علي وضوئه بغيره عثمان وفعله ناس من كبار التابعين كما في العيني على البخاري. قوله: (لتحصيل العزيمة مراده بها الشيء الأقوى، وليس مراده بها الحكم الذي لم يبن على أعذار العباد، فإن التلفظ بها لم يرد عن الشارع قوله : (أي) المنقول عن النبي ، والصحابة،
Chapter on the etiquettes of wudu: fourteen things, and more have been added. 'Adab' is the plural of 'adab', and it is defined as putting things in their proper places, or it is said praiseworthy traits, or piety. In Sharh al-Hidayah, it is what the Prophet (peace be upon him) did once or twice and did not consistently practice; its ruling is reward for doing it and no blame for leaving it. As for sunnah, it is what the Prophet consistently practiced, while leaving it without excuse once or twice; its ruling is reward, and for leaving it there is reproach but no punishment. So the etiquettes of wudu are: sitting in an elevated place to protect against splashes, facing the qiblah except when performing istinja, because that is a state more hopeful for acceptance of supplication, placing the small vessel on the left and the large one from which he takes water on the right, not seeking help from others to perform the worship himself without assistance without excuse, not speaking with people's speech because it distracts from the well-known supplications without necessity, combining the intention of the heart with the action of the tongue to attain resolution, supplicating with what is narrated from the Prophet, his Companions, and the Followers, and saying the basmalah and intention while washing each limb... His statement: 'and more have been added' — it reaches in al-Khaza'in to some sixty-odd, as al-Sayyid said. His statement: 'or it is said piety, or it is said what is better to do than leave, or it is said what the responsible person is praised for and not blamed for leaving, or it is said what is demanded legally without blame for leaving' — all are close. His statement: 'it is what the Prophet did, etc.' — it is called nafil because it is extra to the obligatory, mustahab because the Lawgiver loves it, mandub because the Lawgiver has shown its reward, and tatawwu' because the doer volunteers it — said by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'As for sunnah' — meaning the emphasized sunnah. His statement: '(no)' punishment, but if one habitually leaves it, there is a slight sin less than the sin of leaving an obligatory act, as mentioned before. His statement: 'sitting in an elevated place' — the meaning is preserving the clothes from used water as al-Kamal mentioned, not restricted to sitting in an elevated place, said by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'because that state is more hopeful for acceptance of supplication' — meaning it includes supplications, and because of the hadith: 'The most honorable of gatherings is that in which the qiblah is faced.' His statement: 'and not seeking help from others' — al-Kirmani said: There is no dislike in pouring, and it is not said it is against the optimal, and he cited several hadith indicating that the Prophet did it, and he weakened what indicates dislike, and among those who sought help in his wudu was Uthman, and many of the great Followers did so, as in al-Ayni on Bukhari. His statement: 'to attain resolution' — his intention is a stronger thing, not the ruling that is not based on excuses of the servants, for verbalizing it is not reported from the Lawgiver. His statement: 'that is' reported from the Prophet and the Companions...
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the etiquettes (adab) of wudu, providing a definition and listing fourteen items. The text distinguishes adab from sunnah: adab is what the Prophet did once or twice without consistency, rewarded but no blame for leaving; sunnah is what he consistently did, rewarded but leaving it brings reproach (not punishment). The list includes sitting in a high place, facing qiblah (except during istinja), placing vessels appropriately, not seeking help without excuse, not speaking worldly words, combining heart intention with verbal expression, supplicating with transmitted prayers, and saying tasmiyah (bismillah) and intention while washing each limb. The commentary expands on the definition, noting that the number of adab is extended in some sources to over sixty. It also clarifies that 'not seeking help' is not disliked, as the Prophet himself allowed it. The ruling on verbalizing the intention is discussed: it is not a requirement from the Lawgiver, but a means to strengthen resolve. The passage is definitional and ruling in nature, as it explains what adab are and provides examples. The authority weight is from later commentary (Sharh al-Hidayah) and fatawa, as the matn is not from Zahir al-Riwayah but a later compilation.

Key Terms
أدب (adab (plural: adab)): Etiquette: acts done by the Prophet once or twice without consistency; rewarded but no blame for leaving.
السنة (al-sunnah): Prophetic practice done consistently; rewarded, leaving without excuse brings reproach.
العزيمة (al-'azimah): Resolution or a stronger thing; the commentator says it means a stronger thing, not the legal ruling based on excuses.
مندوب (mandub): An act the Lawgiver has shown its reward; synonym of mustahab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between adab and sunnah according to the definition in this passage?
A) Adab are obligatory, sunnah is optional
B) Adab are done consistently, sunnah inconsistently
C) Adab are done inconsistently with reward and no blame for leaving, sunnah is done consistently with reward and reproach for leaving
D) There is no difference

Key Takeaway
Adab in wudu are recommended practices that earn reward but carry no blame for omission, distinguishing them from the more binding sunnah.

Supplications and Etiquettes of Wudu
List of recommended duas and etiquettes with hadith authenticity discussion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended duas and physical etiquettes during wudu, and identify the correct phrasing for narrating weak hadith regarding virtues.

Core Idea
Wudu duas and adab are sunnah mu'akkadah; weak hadith on virtues are permissible with tentative phrasing.

This lesson from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details the recommended supplications for each wudu action and the physical etiquettes, such as using the right hand for rinsing and inserting the little finger into the ears. It also addresses an important hadith methodology: how to narrate weak hadith in the context of virtues, emphasizing the use of cautious phrases like 'ruwiya' instead of definitive statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended duas for each limb
Read the Arabic text and find the supplication for rinsing the mouth, snuffing water, washing face, hands, wiping head, ears, neck, and washing feet. Note that they begin with 'Bismillah' followed by a specific dua.
The duas are for enhancing the spiritual reward, not for validity.
2
List the physical etiquettes (adab) of wudu
Find the practices: inserting the little finger into the ear canals, moving a wide ring to ensure water reaches the skin, using the right hand for rinsing and snuffing, and the left for blowing the nose. Also note the recommendation to perform wudu before the time for non-excused persons.
These are sunnah mu'akkadah; omitting them does not invalidate wudu.
3
Understand the hadith methodology regarding weak narrations
Read the commentator's discussion: the supplications' hadith are weak, but scholars act upon them in virtues. When narrating a weak hadith, one must use tentative phrases (siyagh al-tamrid) like 'ruwiya' (it is narrated) rather than definitive statements like 'qala Rasulullah'.
This is to avoid attributing falsehood to the Prophet (SAW).
4
Apply the ruling: distinguish between strong and weak hadith phrasing
For authentic hadith, use definitive phrases (e.g., 'qala'). For weak or doubtful hadith, use tentative phrases. This principle applies to all narrations, not just wudu.
The only confirmed narration from the Prophet regarding wudu is the two shahadahs after completion.

Source Text
