كتاب الطهارة
المضمضة: باسم الله اللهم أعني على تلاوة القرآن ،وذكرك وشكرك وحسن عبادتك وعند الاستنشاق باسم الله اللهم أرحني رائحة الجنة ولا ترحني رائحة النار وهكذا في سائره، ويصلي على النبي أيضاً كما في التوضيح (و) من آدابه (إدخال خنصره في صماخ أذنيه) مبالغ في المسح وتحريك خاتمه الواسع للمبالغة في الغسل (و) كون (المضمضة والاستنشاق باليد اليمنى لشرفها إجماعاً والامتخاط باليسرى) لامتهانها (و) تقديم التوضؤ قبل دخول الوقت مبادرة للطاعة (لغير المعذور) لأن وضوءه ينتقض بخروج
والتابعين قال ابن أمير حاج : سئل شيخنا حافظ عصره شهاب الدین بن حجر العسقلاني عن الأحاديث التي ذكرت في مقدمة أبي الليث في أدعية الأعضاء، فأجاب بأنها ضعيفة والعلماء يتساهلون في ذكر الحديث الضعيف والعمل به في الفضائل، ولم يثبت منها شيء عن رسول الله لا من قوله ولا من فعله أهـ وطرقها كلها لا تخلو عن متهم بوضع، ونسبة هذه الأدعية إلى السلف الصالح، أولى من نسبتها إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حذراً من الوقوع في مصداق من كذب علي متعمداً فليتبوأ مقعده من النار، وعن هذا قالوا كما في التقريب، وشرحه : إذا أردت رواية حديث ضعيف بغير إسناد، فلا تقل قال رسول الله ، وما أشبه ذلك من صيغ الجزم، بل قل روي عنه ،كذا، أو بلغنا أو ورد أو جاء أو نقل، وما أشبهه من صيغ التمريض، وكذا فيما تشك في صحته، وضعفه أما الصحيح، فاذكره بصيغة الجزم، ويقيح فيه صيغة التمريض كما يقبح في الضعيف صيغة الجزم قال الهندي وغيره: ولم يثبت منه إلا الشهادتان بعد الفراغ منه قاله السيد عن النهر قوله (والنية) أي إستصحابها كما في الفتح، وأشار بقوله إستصحابها إلى أن المنوي واحد وهو إمتثال الأمر مثلاً. قوله: (وهكذا في سائرها) فيقول عند غسل الوجه : باسم الله اللهم بيض وجهي يوم تبيض وجوه وتسود وجوه، وعند غسل اليمنى باسم الله اللهم أعطني كتابي بيميني، وحاسبني حساباً يسيراً، وعند غسل اليسرى باسم الله اللهم لا تعطني كتابي بشمالي ولا من وراء ظهري، وعند مسح رأسه باسم الله اللهم أظلني تحت ظل عرشك يوم لا ظل إلا ظل عرشك، وعند مسح ا أذنيه باسم الله اللهم اجعلني من الذين يستمعون القول فيتبعون أحسنه، عنقه باسم الله اللهم أعتق رقبتي من النار، وعند غسل رجله اليمنى باسم الله اللهم ثبت قدمي على الصراط يوم تزل الأقدام، وعند غسل اليسرى باسم الله اللهم اجعل ذنبي مغفوراً وسعيي مشكوراً، وتجارتي لن تبور اهـ من الشرح. قوله: (أيضاً) أي بعد كل دعاء. قوله : (وإدخال خنصره) أي أنملة خنصره، وهو بكسر الخاء، والصاد وقال الفارسي الفصيح فتح الصاد. قال في المحيط : ويدخل خنصره في صماخ أذنيه ويحركها، وهو مروي عن أبي يوسف والصماخان مثنى صماخ بكسر الصاد، ويقال : بالسين المهملة قوله : ( وتحريك خاتمه الواسع أما الضيق فإن علم وصول الماء استحب تحريكه، والإفتراض قاله السيد قوله : (والإمتخاط) مثله الإستنشار.
Book of Purification. Rinsing the mouth: [say] 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, help me to recite the Qur'an, and remember You, and thank You, and worship You well.' And when snuffing water: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, let me smell the fragrance of Paradise and do not let me smell the fire of Hell.' And similarly for the rest, and he also sends blessings on the Prophet as in al-Tawdih. (And) among its etiquettes: (inserting his little finger into the ear canal) exaggerating in wiping, and moving his wide ring to exaggerate in washing. (And) that (rinsing the mouth and snuffing water should be done with the right hand due to its honor by consensus, and blowing the nose with the left) because it is undignified. (And) performing wudu before the time enters as an eager act of obedience (for the non-excused person) because his wudu is invalidated by the exit of the time. And the Successors. Ibn Amir Haj said: Our shaykh, the hafiz of his age, Shihab al-Din ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, was asked about the hadiths mentioned in the introduction of Abu al-Layth regarding the supplications for the limbs, and he answered that they are weak, and scholars are lenient in mentioning weak hadith and acting upon them in virtues, and nothing of them is confirmed from the Messenger of Allah, either in his words or his actions. Their chains all contain an accused forger. Attributing these supplications to the righteous predecessors is better than attributing them to the Messenger of Allah, to avoid falling into the meaning of 'whoever lies about me intentionally, let him take his seat in the Fire.' For this reason, they said, as in al-Taqrib and its commentary: If you want to narrate a weak hadith without an isnad, do not say 'The Messenger of Allah said' or similar definitive phrases, but rather say 'It is narrated from him' or 'it has reached us' or 'it has come' or 'it is transmitted' and similar phrases of uncertainty. Likewise for what you doubt its authenticity. As for the authentic, mention it with a definitive phrase, and it is ugly to use a phrase of uncertainty for it just as it is ugly to use a definitive phrase for the weak. Al-Hindi and others said: Nothing has been confirmed from it except the two shahadahs after completing wudu, as al-Sayyid said from al-Nahr. His saying (intention) meaning its maintenance as in al-Fath. And by his saying 'its maintenance' he indicated that the intended thing is one, for example, compliance with the command. His saying: 'And similarly for the rest' he says when washing the face: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, whiten my face on the day when faces are whitened and blackened.' When washing the right hand: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, give me my book in my right hand, and make my account easy.' When washing the left hand: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, do not give me my book in my left hand or from behind my back.' When wiping his head: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, shade me under the shade of Your Throne on the day when there is no shade but the shade of Your Throne.' When wiping his ears: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, make me among those who listen to speech and follow the best of it.' His neck: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, free my neck from the Fire.' When washing his right foot: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, keep my foot firm on the Straight Path on the day when feet slip.' When washing his left foot: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, make my sin forgiven, my effort thanked, and my trade never perish.' End from the commentary. His saying: 'also' meaning after every supplication. His saying: 'and inserting his little finger' meaning the fingertip of his little finger, with kasra on the kha' and sad, but al-Farisi said the eloquent is fatha on the sad. He said in al-Muhit: And he inserts his little finger into the ear canal and moves it, and it is narrated from Abu Yusuf. The two ear canals are dual of 'samakh' with kasr on the sad, and it is said with sin. His saying: 'and moving his wide ring. As for the tight one, if water reaching is known, moving it is recommended, and the supposition [of water reaching] is [sufficient] as said by al-Sayyid.' His saying: 'and blowing the nose' is similar to snuffing.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a list of recommended acts (adab) for wudu, including specific supplications for each limb and physical etiquettes. The author presents the base matn from Maraqi al-Falah, with commentary from al-Tahtawi. He begins with the supplications for rinsing the mouth and snuffing water, then notes similar supplications for other limbs. A lengthy discussion follows regarding the authenticity of these hadiths, citing Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, who declared them weak but noted scholars act upon them in virtues. The proper manner of narrating weak hadith is explained: one should use tentative phrases like 'it is narrated' rather than definitive 'the Prophet said'. The commentator then returns to the etiquettes: inserting the little finger into the ears for thorough wiping, moving a wide ring to ensure water reaches the skin, using the right hand for rinsing and left for blowing the nose. Finally, the point is made that one should perform wudu before the time (for non-excused persons) as an act of eagerness, though this ruling is elaborated elsewhere.

Key Terms
المضمضة (al-madmadah): Rinsing the mouth during wudu, a sunnah act.
الاستنشاق (al-istinshaq): Snuffing water into the nose during wudu.
صيغ التمريض (siyagh al-tamrid): Phrases indicating uncertainty when narrating hadith, like 'ruwiya' (it is narrated) or 'balaghana' (it reached us).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The adab of wudu are sunnah mu'akkadah, and weak hadith on virtues are permissible with proper cautious phrasing.

Timing of Wudu: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Invalidation
Intra-Hanafi ruling on wudu timeliness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wudu performed before its time and identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar regarding when it becomes invalid.

Core Idea
Wudu before its time is valid but is invalidated by the exit of the time according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The timing of wudu is crucial for prayer validity. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the Hanafi position on performing wudu before its prescribed time and the different views within the school. Understanding these nuances helps avoid incorrect assumptions about wudu invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing wudu before the time of a prayer. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) but time-dependent.
The wudu itself is not invalid simply because it is done early.
2
State the three Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa (and Muhammad): invalidated by exit of time; Zufar: invalidated by entrance; Abu Yusuf: both entrance and exit.
3
Follow the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view, as indicated by the matn saying 'at us'.
Al-Tahtawi confirms this is the madhhab's position.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: According to Abu Hanifa, wudu done before Dhuhr remains valid until Dhuhr time ends; according to Zufar, it becomes invalid as soon as Dhuhr begins; according to Abu Yusuf, both the beginning and end invalidate it.
This affects whether one can pray at the beginning or end of the time with the same wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوقت عندنا وبدخوله عند زفر وبهما عند أبي يوسف والإتيان بالشهادتين بعده) قائماً مستقبلاً لقوله : (ما منكم من أحد يتوضأ فيسبغ الوضوء ثم يقول أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمداً عبده ورسوله وفي رواية (أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله إلا فتحت له أبواب الجنة الثمانية يدخلها من (أي باب شاء) وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من قال إذا توضأ سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك أشهد أن لا إله إلا أنت أستغفرك وأتوب إليك طبع بطابع ثم جعل تحت العرش حتى يؤتى بصاحبها يوم القيامة (وإن يشرب من فضل الوضوء قائماً مستقبل القبلة، أو قاعداً لأنه شرب فضل وضوئه وماء زمزم وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا يشربن أحدكم قائماً فمن نسي فليستقيء
The time according to us and its entrance according to Zufar and both according to Abu Yusuf, and the recitation of the two shahadahs after it) standing facing the qibla, due to his statement: 'There is none among you who performs wudu and completes it, then says: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is His servant and messenger' and in a narration: 'I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and messenger, except that the eight gates of Paradise are opened for him, he enters from whichever gate he wishes.' And the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever says after wudu: Glory be to You, O Allah, and by Your praise, I bear witness that there is no god but You, I seek Your forgiveness and repent to You, it is stamped with a seal, then placed under the Throne until it is brought to its owner on the Day of Resurrection.' (And that he drinks from the leftover water of wudu standing facing the qibla, or sitting, because he drinks the leftover of his wudu and Zamzam water. And the Messenger of Allah said: 'Let none of you drink standing; so if he forgets, let him vomit.'
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the timing of wudu and the recommended dhikr after it. The base matn states that wudu performed before the time is valid but is invalidated by the exit of the time according to the Hanafi school; Zufar says it is invalidated by the entrance of the time, while Abu Yusuf says both entrance and exit invalidate it. The commentator notes that if one performs wudu in a gap between two prayer times, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar. Then the passage deals with the sunnah of reciting the two shahadahs after wudu, citing a hadith from Muslim that the eight gates of Paradise are opened for such a person. Another hadith mentions another supplication that is stamped and placed under the Throne. Finally, it is recommended to drink the leftover water of wudu while standing facing the qibla, though drinking standing is generally prohibited, but an exception is made for this case and for Zamzam water.

Key Terms
فضل الوضوء (fadl al-wudu): The leftover water from wudu.
الإتيان بالشهادتين (al-ityān bi al-shahādatayn): Reciting the two testimonies of faith after wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately
B) At the entrance of the time
C) At the exit of the time
D) It never becomes invalid

Key Takeaway
Wudu before its time is valid and remains so until the prayer time exits according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Recommended Acts After Wudu: Shahadahs, Supplication, and Drinking Leftover Water
Ruling on post-wudu sunnah acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts after wudu and cite the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
After wudu, reciting the shahadahs and a special supplication, and drinking leftover water, are sunnah acts with great rewards.

This passage details the recommended practices immediately after completing wudu. These acts transform wudu from a mere purification into a spiritual opportunity. The hadith promise immense rewards, encouraging consistent practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
The passage mentions three sunnah acts: reciting the two shahadahs, reciting a specific du'a, and drinking the leftover water of wudu.
All are sunnah, not fard or wajib.
2
Note the recommended posture
The shahadahs and du'a are said standing, facing the qibla. Drinking water can be done standing or sitting, but standing is mentioned first.
The standing posture is mustahabb.
3
Examine the hadith for shahadahs
The Prophet said: Whoever performs wudu thoroughly, then says the shahadahs, the eight gates of Paradise are opened for him.
Muslim's narration is cited.
4
Examine the hadith for the du'a
Another hadith: Whoever says this supplication after wudu has it stamped and placed under the Throne until the Day of Resurrection.
This indicates immense reward.
5
Understand the ruling on drinking leftover water
Drinking the leftover water is recommended despite the general prohibition of drinking standing, because of its special virtue akin to Zamzam.
The hadith prohibiting drinking standing is cited, but an exception is made here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوقت عندنا وبدخوله عند زفر وبهما عند أبي يوسف والإتيان بالشهادتين بعده) قائماً مستقبلاً لقوله : (ما منكم من أحد يتوضأ فيسبغ الوضوء ثم يقول أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمداً عبده ورسوله وفي رواية (أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله إلا فتحت له أبواب الجنة الثمانية يدخلها من (أي باب شاء) وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من قال إذا توضأ سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك أشهد أن لا إله إلا أنت أستغفرك وأتوب إليك طبع بطابع ثم جعل تحت العرش حتى يؤتى بصاحبها يوم القيامة (وإن يشرب من فضل الوضوء قائماً مستقبل القبلة، أو قاعداً لأنه شرب فضل وضوئه وماء زمزم وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا يشربن أحدكم قائماً فمن نسي فليستقيء
The time according to us and its entrance according to Zufar and both according to Abu Yusuf, and the recitation of the two shahadahs after it) standing facing the qibla, due to his statement: 'There is none among you who performs wudu and completes it, then says: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is His servant and messenger' and in a narration: 'I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and messenger, except that the eight gates of Paradise are opened for him, he enters from whichever gate he wishes.' And the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever says after wudu: Glory be to You, O Allah, and by Your praise, I bear witness that there is no god but You, I seek Your forgiveness and repent to You, it is stamped with a seal, then placed under the Throne until it is brought to its owner on the Day of Resurrection.' (And that he drinks from the leftover water of wudu standing facing the qibla, or sitting, because he drinks the leftover of his wudu and Zamzam water. And the Messenger of Allah said: 'Let none of you drink standing; so if he forgets, let him vomit.'
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the timing of wudu and the recommended dhikr after it. The base matn states that wudu performed before the time is valid but is invalidated by the exit of the time according to the Hanafi school; Zufar says it is invalidated by the entrance of the time, while Abu Yusuf says both entrance and exit invalidate it. The commentator notes that if one performs wudu in a gap between two prayer times, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar. Then the passage deals with the sunnah of reciting the two shahadahs after wudu, citing a hadith from Muslim that the eight gates of Paradise are opened for such a person. Another hadith mentions another supplication that is stamped and placed under the Throne. Finally, it is recommended to drink the leftover water of wudu while standing facing the qibla, though drinking standing is generally prohibited, but an exception is made for this case and for Zamzam water.

Key Terms
فضل الوضوء (fadl al-wudu): The leftover water from wudu.
الإتيان بالشهادتين (al-ityān bi al-shahādatayn): Reciting the two testimonies of faith after wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Wajib
C) Sunnah muakkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Reciting the shahadahs, the special du'a, and drinking leftover water are sunnah acts after wudu, with immense rewards.

Ruling on Wudu Before Prayer Time: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wudu timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on wudu performed before prayer time and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf/Zufar regarding its validity.

Core Idea
A wudu in the negligible time between prayers is valid according to the majority, but repeating within time avoids ikhtilaf.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whether wudu performed before the entry of prayer time is valid for that prayer. The passage presents three scholarly positions: the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and the dissenting views of Abu Yusuf and Zufar. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the importance of timing in taharah and the recommended practice to avoid disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its temporal context
Determine the act being evaluated: wudu performed before the time of the intended prayer. Note the distinction between cases where there is a 'negligible time' (waqt muhmal) between two prayer times and cases where there is none.
The negligible time is the brief gap, e.g., between Zuhr and Asr.
2
State the three positions
Recognize that the base text states: 'the time according to us' (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), 'with its entry according to Zufar', and 'with both according to Abu Yusuf'. This means for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, wudu is valid before time; for Zufar, it becomes valid only at the entry of time; for Abu Yusuf, both conditions are needed. The commentary clarifies the dispute is about validity if there is a negligible time.
Base text says 'الوقت عندنا'; the commentary expands the ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the conditions for validity
When there is a negligible time, wudu performed in that gap for the next prayer is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (candidate). Abu Yusuf and Zufar disagree (la yajuz). When there is no negligible time, performing wudu at the very end of the first time for the second time is invalid by consensus (ijma').
The consensus case requires repetition as wajib.
4
Determine the recommended practice
To exit the ikhtilaf, it is recommended (tundabu) to repeat the wudu within the actual time of the intended prayer. This preserves the valid opinion while avoiding disagreement.
This is a common principle: istihbab al-khuruj min al-khilaf.
5
Identify the unique cases where nafl is better than fard
The commentator al-Sayyid notes that this is one of three issues where supererogatory (nafl) is better than obligatory (fard). The others: giving respite to a debtor is better than just deferring, and initiating salam is better than returning it.
This highlights the virtue of choosing the more precautionary or virtuous action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة الوقت عندنا وبدخوله عند زفر وبهما عند أبي يوسف والإتيان بالشهادتين بعده) قائماً مستقبلاً لقوله : (ما منكم من أحد يتوضأ فيسبغ الوضوء ثم يقول أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمداً عبده ورسوله وفي رواية (أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله إلا فتحت له أبواب الجنة الثمانية يدخلها من (أي باب شاء) وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من قال إذا توضأ سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك أشهد أن لا إله إلا أنت أستغفرك وأتوب إليك طبع بطابع ثم جعل تحت العرش حتى يؤتى بصاحبها يوم القيامة (وإن يشرب من فضل الوضوء قائماً مستقبل القبلة، أو قاعداً لأنه شرب فضل وضوئه وماء زمزم وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا يشربن أحدكم قائماً فمن نسي فليستقىء كما نص . قائماً من ينتقض الخ) أي وهو إذا توضأ في زمن قبل الوقت، فلا يخلو أما أن يكون بين الوقتين وقت مهمل أولا فإن كان بينهما وقت مهمل وتوضأ فيه للوقت الثاني جاز ذلك عندهما وقال أبو يوسف وزفر : لا يجوز فتندب له إعادة الوضوء في الوقت خروجاً من الخلاف وإن لم يكن بينهما وقت مهمل وتوضأ في آخر الوقت للوقت الثاني لا يجوز إجماعاً فتجب إعادة الوضوء، وحينئذ فلا فائدة في وضوئه قبل الوقت قال السيد : وهذه إحدى المسائل الثلاث التي النفل فيها أفضل من الفرض الثانية إبراء المعسر أفضل من إنظاره الثالثة البدء بالسلام أفضل من رده
The Book of Purification: The time according to us, and with its entry according to Zufar, and with both according to Abu Yusuf, and the recitation of the two testimonies after it) standing, facing the qibla, due to his saying: 'There is none among you who performs wudu and perfects the wudu, then says, "I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is His servant and messenger" — and in another narration, "I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and messenger" — except that the eight gates of Paradise are opened for him, he enters through whichever he wishes.' And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever says, when he performs wudu, "Glory be to You, O Allah, and praise be to You; I bear witness that there is no god but You; I seek Your forgiveness and repent to You," it is stamped with a seal, then placed beneath the Throne until its owner is brought on the Day of Resurrection. And he drinks from the leftover water of wudu standing, facing the qibla, or sitting, because it is drinking the leftover of his wudu and Zamzam water. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Let none of you drink standing; whoever forgets, let him vomit.' As the text states. Standing from the nullifiers) i.e., he is when he performs wudu in a time before the time. So it is either that there is a negligible time between the two times or not. If there is a negligible time between them and he performs wudu in it for the second time, that is permissible according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and Abu Yusuf and Zufar said: it is not permissible, so it is recommended for him to repeat the wudu in the time to exit the disagreement. And if there is no negligible time between them and he performs wudu at the end of the first time for the second time, it is not permissible by consensus, so repeating the wudu is obligatory. Thus, there is no benefit in his wudu before the time. Al-Sayyid said: This is one of the three issues in which supererogatory (nafl) is better than obligatory (fard): the second is giving respite to a debtor in difficulty is better than deferring, the third is initiating the greeting of peace is better than returning it.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling of performing wudu before the time of prayer. The base text states that wudu is valid before the time (according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and that its validity occurs with entry of time according to Zufar, and with both conditions according to Abu Yusuf. The commentator explains that if there is a gap between the two times (e.g., between Zuhr and Asr) and one performs wudu in that gap for the second prayer, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar. To avoid the difference, it is recommended to repeat the wudu within the time. If there is no gap, performing wudu at the very end of the first time for the second prayer is invalid by consensus, requiring repetition. The commentator then notes that this is one of three cases where supererogatory acts are better than obligatory ones, citing two other examples: giving respite to a debtor is better than just deferring, and initiating Salam is better than returning it. The primary dalil for the virtue of wudu and its supplications is the hadith quoted about the gates of Paradise and the special seal under the Throne.

Key Terms
الوقت المهمل (al-waqt al-muhmal): The negligible time between the end of one prayer time and the start of the next.
عندهما (indahuma): According to them both (i.e., Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wudu before the time is better than wudu within the time
B) Giving respite to a debtor is better than deferring
C) Initiating salam is better than returning it
D) Performing wudu with leftover water is better than with fresh water

Key Takeaway
Wudu performed in the negligible time between two prayers is valid according to the majority Hanafi view, but repeating it within the prayer time is recommended to avoid the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

The Recommended Dhikr After Wudu: Shahadatain and Pointing the Finger
Recommended post-wudu dhikr with instructions and virtue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah muakkadah ruling of reciting the shahadatain after wudu and describe the recommended method including pointing the index finger.

Core Idea
Reciting the shahadatain after wudu with a pointed finger opens the eight gates of Paradise.

Completing wudu is a moment of spiritual purity. The Prophet ﷺ taught a beautiful supplication that opens the doors of Paradise. This lesson explores the recommended dhikr after wudu, its proof, and the etiquettes including pointing the finger, rooted in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting the shahadatain (Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan abduhu wa rasuluhu) after completing wudu. According to the Hanafi school, this is a stressed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah).
Not obligatory (fard) but highly recommended.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is a hadith narrated by Muslim: 'Whoever performs wudu, does it perfectly, then says Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah... except that the eight gates of Paradise are opened for him, and he may enter through whichever he wishes.'
This hadith is zanni al-thubut (single transmission) but accepted for virtue.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The promise of entering Paradise indicates the immense reward and encourages this dhikr, establishing it as a recommended sunnah. The word 'except' (illa) shows a conditional link between the dhikr and the reward.
Hanafi usul: a promise of reward typically indicates recommendation, not obligation.
4
Note the additional practice of pointing the finger
Al-Ghaznawi mentions that one should point with the index finger (sabbaba/musabbiha) while looking at the sky when reciting the shahada. This practice is also related to the story of Adam's light.
The finger is called musabbiha (glorifying) due to its association with tawhid.
5
Understand the virtue and seal
The hadith also mentions that this dhikr is 'stamped with a seal' (طبع بطابع) under the Throne, signifying its high status and abundant reward.
The 'seal' emphasizes the acceptance and honor of this dhikr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والإتيان بالشهادتين بعده) ذكر الغزنوي أنه يشير بسبابته حين النظر إلى السماء وسميت سبابة لأنه يسب بها والأولى تسميتها بمسبحة عليه في شرح الشرعة، وخصت بذلك لما ذكره شراح المولد أن الله تعالى لما خلق آدم جعل نور محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم في صلبه فكانت الملائكة تقف خلفه تعظم هذا النور، فسأل آدم ربه عز وجل أن يحوله أمامه حتى تستقبله الملائكة، فجعله في جبهته، ثم قال آدم : اللهم اجعل لي من هذا النور نصيباً فجعله الله تعالى في مسبحته فصار ينظر إليه، وكان كذلك إلى أن نزل الدنيا، واشتغل بأمر المعاش، فجعل في ظهره كما كان أولاً، فأعطيت المسبحة الشرف من وقتئذ، وهذا أولى مما في السيد قوله: (فيسبغ الوضوء) أي يعم الأعضاء بالماء من قولهم درع سابغة أي شاملة للبدن والمراد هنا الإحسان قوله : (وفي رواية) هي لمسلم . قوله : يدخلها من أي باب شاء وذلك لتعظيمه وتكريمه . قوله : (طبع بطابع) أي ختم عليه بخاتم والمقصود بختمه تعظيمه ويترتب عليه كثرة الثواب
His saying: 'And the recitation of the two testimonies after it' – al-Ghaznawi mentioned that he points with his index finger when looking at the sky, and it was called 'sabbaba' because one insults with it; it is better to call it 'musabbiha' as in Sharh al-Shar'a. It was specified with that because, as the commentators of the Mawlid mention, when Allah created Adam, He placed the light of Muhammad (peace be upon him) in his loins, so the angels would stand behind him to honor this light. Adam asked his Lord to move it to his front so the angels would face it, and He placed it in his forehead. Then Adam said, 'O Allah, give me a portion of this light,' so Allah placed it in his 'musabbiha' (index finger), and he would look at it. It remained like that until he descended to the world and became occupied with livelihood, so it was placed in his back as it was originally. Thus, the 'musabbiha' was given honor from that time. This is better than what is in al-Sayyid. His saying: 'He perfects the wudu' means he covers the limbs with water, from their saying 'a full coat of mail' meaning covering the body; here it means excellence. His saying: 'And in a narration' – it is from Muslim. His saying: 'He enters through whichever gate he wishes' – that is for his glorification and honor. His saying: 'It is stamped with a seal' means sealed with a ring; the purpose of sealing it is its glorification, and it results in abundant reward.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage explains the recommended act of reciting the shahadatain after wudu. The commentator al-Ghaznawi notes that one should point with the index finger while looking at the sky. The finger is called 'sabbaba' (pointing finger) but it is better to call it 'musabbiha' (glorifying finger) due to a story from the prophets: Adam's light was transferred to various places, and ultimately the index finger was honored with it. The hadith quoted confirms that reciting the shahadatain after performing wudu properly opens all eight gates of Paradise. The seal under the Throne indicates the high status of this dhikr. The commentary also clarifies that 'isbagh al-wudu' means thoroughly washing the limbs, and the narration with 'wahdahu la sharika lah' is from Muslim.

Key Terms
السبابة (al-sabbaba): Index finger, called 'sabbaba' because it is used for pointing and insulting; better called 'musabbiha' due to its association with glorification.
المسبحة (al-musabbiha): Alternative name for index finger, meaning 'the glorifying finger' due to its use in tawhid.
فيسبغ الوضوء (fa yusbighu al-wudu): To perform wudu perfectly, covering all limbs thoroughly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One's sins are forgiven.
B) The eight gates of Paradise are opened for him.
C) He is saved from the punishment of the grave.
D) He is granted a palace in Paradise.

Key Takeaway
Reciting the shahadatain after wudu, while pointing the index finger, is a confirmed sunnah with great reward—one should perfect one's wudu and recite them hoping to enter Paradise.

Drinking the Leftover Wudu Water: A Recommended Practice
Etiquette of drinking leftover wudu water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on drinking leftover wudu water and identify the condition under which it is avoided.

Core Idea
Drinking leftover wudu water is a blessed practice, but avoid it if you are fasting.

The text opens with instructions on drinking the leftover water from wudu. It is a recommended act (mustahabb) for those who are not fasting, accompanied by a specific supplication. This simple act carries spiritual and physical benefits, as noted in the Hindiyya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text describes drinking leftover wudu water. Determine the hukm: is it wajib, sunnah, mustahabb, or mubah? The phrasing 'من فضل الوضوء' in the context of adab suggests it is recommended.
2
Note the condition
The text says 'ما لم يكن صائماً' – as long as he is not fasting. This is a condition that restricts the recommendation. If fasting, it is not recommended to drink.
3
Recognize the supplication
The text includes a du'a to be said when drinking: 'O Allah, heal me with Your healing...' This indicates the spiritual dimension of the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله من فضل الوضوء) بفتح الواو، الماء الذي يتوضأ به أي ما لم يكن صائماً. قوله : (أو قاعداً) أو للتخيير قالوا: ويقول عند شربه : اللهم اشفني بشفائك، وداوني بدوائك، واعصمني من الوهن، والأمراض، والأوجاع، وفي الهندية يشرب قطرة من فضل وضوئه. قوله : (لا يشربن أحدكم قائماً) محمول على غير الحالتين السابقتين، والمراد المبالغة في النهي عن هذا الفعل قال قتادة لرواية أنس : فالأكل وأجمع العلماء على كراهته تنزيهاً لأمر طبي لا ديني قوله : (وأجمع العلماء على كراهته تنزيهاً الخ) لا تسلم حكاية الإجماع فإنه لما تعارضت الأحاديث الدالة على النهي، والأحاديث الدالة على الفعل اختلف العلماء في المخلص من التعارض فمن قائل إنّ النهي ناسخ للفعل، ومن قائل بالعكس، ومن قائل إن النهي ليس للتحريم، بل للتنزيه لأنه لأمر طبي لا ديني وفعله لبيان الجواز ذكره ابن أمير حاج
His saying: 'from the leftover of wudu' with fathah on the waw, i.e., the water with which he performs wudu, as long as he is not fasting. His saying: 'or sitting' – 'or' is for choice. They said: and he says when drinking: 'O Allah, heal me with Your healing, cure me with Your cure, and protect me from weakness, illnesses, and pains.' And in al-Hindiyya, he drinks a drop from the leftover of his wudu. His saying: 'Let none of you drink standing' – it is applied to other than the two previous cases, and the intent is exaggeration in prohibition of this action. Qatada said regarding the narration of Anas: '...the food.' And the scholars have consensus on its karahah tanzihan due to a medical matter, not religious. His saying: 'And the scholars have consensus on its karahah tanzihan, etc.' – the narration of consensus is not conceded, because when the hadiths indicating prohibition and the hadiths indicating action conflict, the scholars differed on how to reconcile the contradiction. Some said the prohibition abrogates the action, some said the opposite, and some said the prohibition is not for tahrim but for tanzih because it is a medical matter, not religious, and the action demonstrates permissibility. Mentioned by Ibn Amir Hajj.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage covers the adab of drinking leftover wudu water and the ruling on drinking standing. It is recommended to drink the leftover water while facing the qibla, either standing or sitting, and to recite a specific supplication. However, the hadith 'Let none of you drink standing' is also cited. The commentator explains that this prohibition is understood for other situations, and the scholars have consensus that drinking standing is makruh tanzihan (disliked but not sinful) due to medical harm, not religious prohibition. Some scholars debated whether the prohibition is abrogated or not, but the relied-upon view is that it is makruh tanzihan, and the Prophet's own action of drinking standing shows permissibility. Thus, the ruling is not haram.

Key Terms
فضل الوضوء (fadl al-wudu): The leftover water after performing wudu.
كراهة تنزيهاً (karahah tanzihan): Disliked but not sinful; avoiding it is virtuous but doing it is not punishable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, drinking leftover wudu water is recommended except when?
A) The person is standing
B) The person is fasting
C) The person has already drunk water
D) The person is in a state of impurity

Key Takeaway
Drinking leftover wudu water is a recommended practice with a supplication, but it is not recommended for a fasting person.

Drinking While Standing: The Ruling of Karahah Tanzih
Ruling on drinking standing with proof and critique

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why drinking standing is makruh tanzih in the Hanafi school and identify the evidence used to reach this conclusion.

Core Idea
The Prophet's prohibition of drinking standing is interpreted as medical advice, not a religious command, so it is disliked but not sinful.

The hadith 'Let none of you drink standing' seems to forbid, but the Hanafi school, after examining conflicting evidence and medical reasoning, classifies it as makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful). This lesson explores the proof texts, the ikhtilaf among scholars, and the final mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary dalil
The hadith 'لا يشربن أحدكم قائماً' is the main evidence. Determine its type (Sunnah ahad) and its thubut and dalala.
The hadith is ahad, so zanni in transmission and meaning.
2
Analyze the conflicting evidence
There are also hadiths where the Prophet drank standing. This creates a ta'arud (contradiction) that scholars reconciled in different ways.
Some said abrogation, some said the prohibition is not for tahrim.
3
Understand the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school gives precedence to the permissibility hadiths and interprets the prohibition as medical advice (karih tanzihi). Why?
Because the prohibition is for a medical reason, not religious, so it does not reach tahrim.
4
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is makruh tanzih, as supported by Ibn Amir Hajj and other later Hanafi authorities.
The text critiques the claim of consensus, showing that earlier scholars differed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله من فضل الوضوء) بفتح الواو، الماء الذي يتوضأ به أي ما لم يكن صائماً. قوله : (أو قاعداً) أو للتخيير قالوا: ويقول عند شربه : اللهم اشفني بشفائك، وداوني بدوائك، واعصمني من الوهن، والأمراض، والأوجاع، وفي الهندية يشرب قطرة من فضل وضوئه. قوله : (لا يشربن أحدكم قائماً) محمول على غير الحالتين السابقتين، والمراد المبالغة في النهي عن هذا الفعل قال قتادة لرواية أنس : فالأكل وأجمع العلماء على كراهته تنزيهاً لأمر طبي لا ديني قوله : (وأجمع العلماء على كراهته تنزيهاً الخ) لا تسلم حكاية الإجماع فإنه لما تعارضت الأحاديث الدالة على النهي، والأحاديث الدالة على الفعل اختلف العلماء في المخلص من التعارض فمن قائل إنّ النهي ناسخ للفعل، ومن قائل بالعكس، ومن قائل إن النهي ليس للتحريم، بل للتنزيه لأنه لأمر طبي لا ديني وفعله لبيان الجواز ذكره ابن أمير حاج
His saying: 'from the leftover of wudu' with fathah on the waw, i.e., the water with which he performs wudu, as long as he is not fasting. His saying: 'or sitting' – 'or' is for choice. They said: and he says when drinking: 'O Allah, heal me with Your healing, cure me with Your cure, and protect me from weakness, illnesses, and pains.' And in al-Hindiyya, he drinks a drop from the leftover of his wudu. His saying: 'Let none of you drink standing' – it is applied to other than the two previous cases, and the intent is exaggeration in prohibition of this action. Qatada said regarding the narration of Anas: '...the food.' And the scholars have consensus on its karahah tanzihan due to a medical matter, not religious. His saying: 'And the scholars have consensus on its karahah tanzihan, etc.' – the narration of consensus is not conceded, because when the hadiths indicating prohibition and the hadiths indicating action conflict, the scholars differed on how to reconcile the contradiction. Some said the prohibition abrogates the action, some said the opposite, and some said the prohibition is not for tahrim but for tanzih because it is a medical matter, not religious, and the action demonstrates permissibility. Mentioned by Ibn Amir Hajj.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage covers the adab of drinking leftover wudu water and the ruling on drinking standing. It is recommended to drink the leftover water while facing the qibla, either standing or sitting, and to recite a specific supplication. However, the hadith 'Let none of you drink standing' is also cited. The commentator explains that this prohibition is understood for other situations, and the scholars have consensus that drinking standing is makruh tanzihan (disliked but not sinful) due to medical harm, not religious prohibition. Some scholars debated whether the prohibition is abrogated or not, but the relied-upon view is that it is makruh tanzihan, and the Prophet's own action of drinking standing shows permissibility. Thus, the ruling is not haram.

Key Terms
فضل الوضوء (fadl al-wudu): The leftover water after performing wudu.
كراهة تنزيهاً (karahah tanzihan): Disliked but not sinful; avoiding it is virtuous but doing it is not punishable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Haram
B) Makruh tahrimi
C) Makruh tanzih
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Drinking standing is makruh tanzih in the Hanafi school, based on interpreting the hadith prohibition as medical advice rather than a religious command.

The Supplication After Wudu: Seeking Repentance and Purity
Explanation of the recommended du'a after wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the recommended supplication after wudu, explain its meaning, and state why the order of the two phrases is significant.

Core Idea
The du'a after wudu asks Allah to make you among the repentant and the pure—both are loved by Allah.

After completing wudu, the Hanafi school recommends a beautiful du'a asking Allah to include us among the frequently repentant (tawwabin) and the purified (muttahirin). This lesson unpacks the meaning of these two groups, the wisdom behind their order, and the preferred timing of this supplication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting a specific du'a after wudu. The Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
The du'a is not a pillar of wudu; omitting it does not invalidate wudu.
2
Understand the meaning of 'tawwabin'
The word 'tawwab' is an intensive form meaning one who repents frequently, turning away from every sin. It is also an attribute of Allah (the Acceptor of repentance).
The intensive form indicates repeated or complete repentance.
3
Understand the meaning of 'muttahirin'
The word 'muttahirin' refers to those who purify themselves from indecencies and sins—spiritually pure individuals.
Physical purity (wudu) is a prerequisite, but the du'a asks for spiritual purity.
4
Analyze the order of the two phrases
The commentator explains that 'tawwabin' is mentioned before 'muttahirin' to give hope to the sinner (repelling despair) and to prevent the pure person from falling into self-admiration.
This is a profound pedagogical wisdom in the du'a's structure.
5
Note the preferred timing
The du'a may be said during wudu or after, but the preferred method is to say it after completing wudu, connected to the two testimonies (shahadatain).
This is based on what is transmitted from practice, as stated by Ibn Amir Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن يقول اللهم اجعلني من التوابين) أي الراجعين عن كل ذنب والتواب مبالغة وقيل : هو الذي كلما أذنب بادر بالتوبة والتواب من صفات الله تعالى أيضاً لأنه يرجع بالإنعام على كل مذنب بقبول توبته (واجعلني من المتطهرين) أي المتنزهين عن الفواحش، وقدم المذنب على المتظهر لدفع القنوط، والعجب قوله: (أي الراجعين من كل ذنب فالمبالغة فيه من حيث الإعراض عن كل ذنب قوله: (وقيل هو الذي الخ) في هذا المعنى زيادة المبادرة قوله : ( بقبول توبته) متعلق بالأنعام، والباء للتصوير، أو للسببية، ولو زاد واو أو عطفه على الأنعام لكان أولى، وأفاد بعضهم أن التواب في حقه تعالى بمعنى الموفق لها، والذي يقبلها قوله : أي) المتنزهين عن الفواحش) وقيل: الذين لم يذنبوا، وخيره صاحب المنية بين أن يقوله بعد تمام الوضوء، أو في خلاله، وكلا الأمرين حسن كما قاله ابن أمير حاج قال : غير أن الوارد أن يقوله بعد الفراغ متصلاً بالشهادتين قوله : لدفع القنوط أي من المذنب قوله : ( والعجب) أي من المتطهر فإن قلت إن جعله من أحدهما ينافي . الآخر، أجيب عنه بأن الواو بمعنى أو ولقائل أن يقول : إن القنوط طلبه أن يكون منهم، فهو مندفع بالدعاء لا بالتقديم، والعجب لا يتأتى من الكبائر، وهو لم يذنب أصلاً، أو من الفواحش، وهو متنزه عنها على أن مقام الدعاء لا يقال فيه ذلك فتدبر، ويحتمل أن الضمير في قدم يرجع إلى الله تعالى أي في قوله تعالى: (إن الله يجب التوابين ويحب المتطهرين) [البقرة/ ۲]
And that he says: 'O Allah, make me among the tawwabin' – i.e., those who return from every sin; 'tawwab' is an intensive form. It is also said: it is one who, whenever he sins, hastens to repentance. 'Tawwab' is also among the attributes of Allah Almighty, because He returns with favor to every sinner by accepting his repentance. 'And make me among the muttahirun' – i.e., those who are free from indecencies. He gave precedence to the sinner over the pure to repel despair and self-admiration. His saying: 'i.e., those who return from every sin' – the intensive form is with regard to turning away from every sin. His saying: 'and it is said: it is one who...' – in this meaning is an added element of hastening. His saying: 'by accepting his repentance' – it is related to 'favor' and the ba' is for depiction or causality. If he had added a waw or conjoined it to 'favor', it would have been better. Some scholars indicated that 'tawwab' when applied to Allah means the one who grants success to it, and who accepts it. His saying: 'i.e., those free from indecencies' – and it is said: those who have not sinned. The author of al-Munya gave a choice between saying it after completing wudu or during it, and both are good as Ibn Amir Hajj said. However, what is transmitted is to say it after finishing, connected to the two testimonies. His saying: 'to repel despair' – i.e., despair of the sinner. His saying: 'and self-admiration' – i.e., of the pure. If you say that mentioning both is contradictory, the answer is that the waw means 'or'. And one could say: despair is removed by the du'a, not by precedence, and self-admiration does not come from major sins when one has not sinned at all, or from indecencies when one is free from them. Moreover, the context of du'a does not entertain such criticism, so reflect. It is also possible that the pronoun in 'he gave precedence' refers to Allah, i.e., in His saying: 'Indeed Allah loves the tawwabin and loves the muttahirun' [al-Baqarah: 2].
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage explains the recommended supplication after wudu: 'O Allah, make me among the tawwabin (frequently repentant) and among the muttahirun (purified ones).' The term 'tawwab' is an intensive form for one who repents frequently, and it is also an attribute of Allah meaning the Acceptor of repentance. The order of mention—first the repentant, then the pure—is deliberate: it gives hope to the sinner to avoid despair, and for the pure it prevents self-admiration. The commentator discusses the linguistic details and notes that this du'a may be said during or after wudu, but the preferred way is after completion, connected to the shahadatain. The verse from Surah al-Baqarah is cited as a proof that Allah loves both groups.

Key Terms
التواب (al-tawwab): The one who turns back to Allah frequently in repentance, or Allah's attribute as the Acceptor of repentance.
المتطهرين (al-muttahirin): Those who purify themselves from sins and indecencies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the word 'tawwabin' mentioned before 'muttahirin' in this du'a?
A) Because repentance is more important than purity
B) To give hope to the sinner and prevent despair, and to prevent self-admiration in the pure
C) To follow the order of the Quran
D) Because the Prophet preferred it that way

Key Takeaway
The recommended du'a after wudu asks to be among the repentant and the pure, with the order designed to give hope and prevent pride.

Three Disliked Acts in Wudu: Sun-Heated Water, Monopolizing Vessel, Drying Limbs
Rulings on three disliked acts related to wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the Hanafi ruling for three disliked acts in wudu: using sun-heated water, monopolizing a vessel, and drying the limbs.

Core Idea
Three acts in wudu are disliked (makruh tanzih): using sun-heated water, monopolizing a vessel, and drying the limbs.

The Hanafi school is built on ease (samhah) and opposes practices that cause hardship or self-centeredness. In this passage from Hashiyah al-Tahtawi, we encounter three actions that are discouraged during wudu: using water heated by the sun, keeping a vessel exclusively for oneself, and deliberately drying the limbs after wudu. Each is supported by a proof—a hadith, a saying of a pious predecessor, or an athar from the Salaf. Let's analyze these one by one.

Guided Path
1
Identify each disliked act and its ruling
Name the three actions: using sun-heated water, monopolizing a vessel, and drying limbs after wudu. The ruling for all three in the Hanafi school is makruh tanzih (disliked, but not sinful).
The Arabic terms: ماء مشمس, استخلاص, ترك التجفيف.
2
Locate the dalil for each act
For sun-heated water, the proof is a hadith: the Prophet told Aisha not to use it because it causes leprosy. For monopolizing a vessel, the proof is the hadith that Allah loves the tolerant Hanifiyyah, and the action of Muhammad ibn Wasi' preferring public water. For drying limbs, the proof is an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i via Abu Hanifa that one wipes his face and does not dry it.
The hadith for sun-heated water is weak in transmission but accepted by Hanafi fuqaha for virtue guidance.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
The prohibition 'la taf'ali' with a medical cause indicates avoidance (karahah tanzih). For monopolizing, the emphasis on ease (samhah) makes exclusivity against the spirit of shariah. For drying, the practice of the Salaf (leaving wet) indicates drying is a disliked innovation.
None.
4
Note any cross-madhhab differences
Other schools may not consider sun-heated water disliked if the harm is unproven; monopolizing and drying limbs are more uniquely Hanafi. However, the ruling remains within the scope of adab and taharah.
The passage itself does not detail ikhtilaf, but the hanafi_position_box mentions mukhtalaf fih status.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
In daily wudu: avoid using water left in metal or dark containers under the sun; share the water vessel rather than claiming it as personal; after wudu, let limbs air-dry rather than wiping them with a towel. Doing these acts does not invalidate wudu but reduces reward.
The rule is specific to conditions where the water is heated by the sun in containers that transmit heat; modern heating methods may be different.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (إنه لا يتوضأ بماء مشمس لقوله عليه السلام لعائشة حين سخنت الماء : لا تفعلي يا حميراء، فإنه يورث البرص، اهـ من الشرح قوله : (ولا يستخلص لنفسه إناء الخ أي لا يجعله لنفسه خالصاً. الشركة، فقد سئل محمد بن واسع : أي الوضوأين أحب إليك أمن ماء مخمر، أو من متوضأ العامة ؟ قال : من متوضأ العامة قال عليه السلام: إن أحب الأديان إلى الله تعالى السمحة الحنفية اهـ من الشرح قوله : ( حنيفية) أي مائلة عن الأديان الباطلة. قوله : (سمحة) . معنى سهلة، أو معناه مقبولة مرغوب فيها أي ومن سهولتها عدم الإستخلاص. قوله: (وترك التجفيف) في آثار محمد أخبرنا أبو حنيفة عن حماد عن إبراهيم في الرجل يتوضأ فيمسح وجهه يرجع إلى
His saying: 'He does not perform wudu with sun-heated water' because of his (peace be upon him) saying to Aisha when she heated water: 'Do not do that, O Humayra, for it causes leprosy.' End from the Sharh. His saying: 'And he does not monopolize a vessel for himself, etc.' – i.e., he does not make it exclusively for himself. The corporation? Muhammad ibn Wasi' was asked: 'Which of the two wudus do you prefer: from a covered water, or from the public wudu area?' He said: 'From the public wudu area.' He (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, the most beloved of religions to Allah is the tolerant Hanifiyyah.' End from the Sharh. His saying: 'Hanifiyyah' – i.e., inclining away from false religions. His saying: 'Tolerant' – meaning easy, or meaning accepted and desirable. That includes from its ease is not monopolizing. His saying: 'And leaving off drying' – in the Athar of Muhammad: Abu Hanifa informed us from Hammad from Ibrahim regarding a man who performs wudu and wipes his face... it returns to...
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage discusses three acts that are disliked or cautioned against in the context of wudu. First, using water that has been heated by the sun (mushammas) is disliked because the Prophet told Aisha that it causes leprosy. Second, a person should not monopolize a vessel for his own exclusive use when others might benefit from it, as the Hanifiyyah religion is easy and inclusive. The example of Muhammad ibn Wasi' preferring to use the public water source highlights the virtue of sharing. Third, the text mentions 'tark al-tajfif' (not drying) the limbs after wudu, based on an athar from Abu Hanifa from Hammad from Ibrahim that a man performing wudu wipes his face (and does not dry it), indicating that drying the limbs after wudu is disliked.

Key Terms
ماء مشمس (ma' mushammas): Water heated by the sun in a metal or dark container; considered disliked for wudu.
الاستخلاص (al-istikhlas): Monopolizing or making something exclusively for oneself.
ترك التجفيف (tark al-tajfif): Leaving the limbs wet after wudu, not wiping them dry.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that wudu should be performed with ease and sharing, avoiding harmful or monopolistic practices.

Drying After Wudu: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling on drying after wudu with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on drying after wudu and apply the conditions that change its legal classification (permissible, recommended, obligatory).

Core Idea
Drying after wudu is permissible, not disliked, but may become wajib if needed.

In this lesson, we examine the recommended act of drying after wudu. The passage clarifies that drying is generally permissible without dislike, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the views of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. However, the ruling can shift to recommended or even obligatory depending on necessity. We will unpack the evidence and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is drying (tajfif) after wudu. The Hanafi school holds it is permissible (mubah) without dislike, as stated in the text: 'لا بأس به'.
The text contrasts with those who consider it disliked.
2
Examine the evidence for permissibility
Multiple hadiths report that the Prophet (peace be upon him) dried himself after wudu and ghusl. The commentary cites this as the correct view (al-sahih).
The evidence is from practice (fi'l), not explicit command.
3
Understand the condition of exaggeration
The text advises not to exaggerate (لا يبالغ) nor to remove all traces of water, leaving some effect of wudu on the limbs.
This preserves the sunnah of leaving some wetness.
4
Apply the condition of need
If there is a need (hajah) such as extreme cold or illness, drying may become recommended (mustahabb) or even obligatory (wajib) to prevent harm.
The ruling shifts based on the incidental need.
5
Distinguish between living and deceased
For the deceased, drying is recommended so the shroud does not become wet and cling to the body.
This is from the words of our shaykhs (Hanafi scholars).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

إنّه يغسل الذراعين لنصف العضدين، والرجلين لنصف الساقين اهـ. قوله: استعداداً لوقت (آخر) لو قال لوضوء آخر لكان أولى ليعم الوضوء على الوضوء في وقت واحد قوله : ( لقوله الله الخ) أخرجه الديلمي في مسند الفردوس، قوله: (كتب في ديوان الشهداء الديوان بالكسر ويفتح مجمع الصحف، والكتاب يكتب فيه أهل الجيش، وأهل العطية، وأوّل من وضعه عمر رضي الله عنه قاموس فالمراد أنه يكتب اسمه مع أسمائهم في محل كتابتهم، والمراد منه ومما قبله أن يعطي ثوابهم وإن تفاوتت الكيفيات. قوله: (حشره الله محشر (الأنبياء بكسر الشين وتفتح محل الإجتماع أي، وإذا إجتمع معهم في مجمعهم لا يضام لأن مصاحب الكرام لا يضام . قوله: (ولما ذكره الفقيه أبو الليث في مقدمته ذكره المصنف في كبيره قال في المقاصد الحسنة : حديث قراءة إنا أنزلناه عقب الوضوء لا أصل له انتهى ويعني به ما ذكر في المقدمة ولفظه يدل على وضعه.
And drying with a cloth, even if wiping, do not exaggerate. And that his vessel be of clay. And washing its handle three times, and placing it on his left, and placing the hand during washing on its handle, not its head. And tending to his watch-straps and what is under the ring. And exceeding the limits of the obligatory acts to lengthen the blaze (al-ghurrah) and filling his vessel in preparation for another time. And reciting Surat al-Qadr three times due to his saying: Whoever recites after his wudu 'Inna anzalnahu fi laylat al-qadr' once will be among the truthful, and whoever recites it twice will be recorded in the register of martyrs, and whoever recites it three times, Allah will gather him in the gathering-place of the prophets. Reported by al-Daylami, and as mentioned by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth in his introduction. By a cloth: He said: there is no harm in it, said by Muhammad, and we adopt it and see no harm in that, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa. End. And in al-Haniyya: There is no harm for the one performing wudu or ghusl to wipe with a handkerchief; it is reported from the Messenger of Allah that he used to do that, and it is correct, except that one should not exaggerate nor seek to remove all traces, leaving some effect of wudu on the limbs. End. Summarized. And several hadiths have been reported that he did that. All this if there is no need for drying; if there is need, then apparently there is no disagreement about its permissibility without dislike, rather it is recommended or obligatory depending on that incidental need that is repelled by it. Ibn Amir Haj said: Then he said: This is for the living; as for the dead, the implication of the words of our shaykhs is that it is recommended so that his shrouds do not become wet and thus become like him. End. His saying: (and that his vessel be of clay) because it is reported that the angels visit the house of a Muslim whose vessel is of clay. His saying: (and washing its handle three times) to be certain of purity. His saying: (and placing it on his left) so that he pours from it onto his right, and it preceded that which indicates this. His saying: (not its head) to avoid dripping of used water. And his saying: (state of washing) meaning the state of intending to pour for washing, and it is not apparent in the actual state of washing because the hands are busy washing the limbs. His saying: (and what is under the ring) preceded that which indicates it. His saying: (to lengthen the blaze (al-ghurrah)) meaning that which includes the tahjil, and lengthening the ghurrah is by increasing beyond the defined limit as in al-Bahr. As for al-tahjil, he said in Sharh al-Shir'a: That he washes the forearms up to half of the upper arms, and the feet up to half of the calves. End. His saying: (in preparation for another time) it would have been better if he said 'for another wudu' to include wudu upon wudu at one time. His saying: (due to his saying) reported by al-Daylami in Musnad al-Firdaws. His saying: (recorded in the register of martyrs) al-diwan (with kasr and fatah) is the collection of scrolls, and the book in which the army and those receiving stipends are recorded, and the first to establish it was Umar. So the meaning is that his name is written with their names in their writing place. And the intended meaning from this and what preceded is that he is given their reward even if the qualities differ. His saying: (Allah will gather him in the gathering-place of the prophets) with kasr of the shin and fat-h as the place of gathering; i.e., when he gathers with them in their gathering place, he will not be harmed because the companion of noble ones is not harmed. His saying: (and as mentioned by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth in his introduction) the author mentioned it in his big book. He said in al-Maqasid al-Hasana: The hadith of reciting 'Inna anzalnahu' after wudu has no basis, meaning what was mentioned in the introduction, and its wording indicates its fabrication.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiyah) on the recommended acts (adab) of wudu as outlined in Maraqi al-Falah. The commentator expands on each act, providing proofs and clarifications. The first act is drying with a cloth after wudu: it is permissible, not disliked, as adopted from Muhammad and Abu Hanifa. However, exaggeration in drying is discouraged to leave some trace of wudu. If there is a need (e.g., cold weather), it becomes recommended or even obligatory. For the deceased, drying is recommended to avoid wetting the shroud. Second, the vessel should be of clay because angels visit such homes. Third, the handle should be washed three times to ensure purity. Fourth, the vessel should be placed on the left hand so that water may be poured with the right. Fifth, during washing, one should hold the handle, not the head, to avoid drips of used water. Sixth, one should attend to watch-straps and under the ring to ensure water reaches those areas. Seventh, one should exceed the obligatory limits by washing beyond the elbows and ankles to achieve the 'blaze' (ghurrah) and 'tahjil'—the latter meaning washing half the upper arms and half the calves. Eighth, filling the vessel in advance for another wudu is recommended, even for consecutive wudus. Ninth, reciting Surat al-Qadr three times after wudu brings great reward, though the hadith is considered weak by some scholars. The commentator discusses the hadith's authenticity, noting that al-Daylami reported it but al-Maqasid al-Hasana deems it baseless. Overall, these acts are sunnah, not obligatory, but performing them earns reward and perfection in worship.

Key Terms
تجفيف (tajfif): Drying the washed limbs with a cloth after wudu

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on drying after wudu when there is no need?
A) Obligatory (wajib)
B) Permissible (mubah)
C) Disliked (makruh)
D) Forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
Drying after wudu is permissible in the Hanafi school, with the ruling shifting to recommended or obligatory if there is a genuine need.

beginner

Sunan of the Water Vessel and Body Parts in Wudu
List of sunan related to vessel and body parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunan related to the water vessel (clay, washing handle, placement) and attending to watch-straps and rings, and apply them in practice.

Core Idea
The water vessel should be of clay, its handle washed, placed on the left, and one should not hold its head; also attend to watch-straps and rings.

This lesson explores the recommended acts (sunan) concerning the water vessel used for wudu and the care for covered body parts. The passage details that the vessel should be of clay, its handle washed three times, placed on the left hand, and that one should hold the handle not the head to avoid dripping used water. Additionally, one must ensure water reaches under watch-straps and rings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the vessel and its material
The vessel should be of clay (khazaf) because angels visit the house of a Muslim whose vessel is of clay.
This is a recommended sunnah, not obligatory.
2
Washing the handle three times
The handle (urwah) of the vessel should be washed three times to ensure certainty of purity.
Three times is a sunnah for thoroughness.
3
Correct placement of the vessel
Place the vessel on the left hand so that water can be poured onto the right hand.
This facilitates using the right hand for pouring.
4
How to hold the vessel during washing
Place the hand on the handle (urwah), not the head of the vessel, to avoid dripping of used water back into the vessel.
This is to prevent contamination of the remaining water.
5
Tending to watch-straps and rings
Ensure water reaches under watch-straps and rings. This is part of the sunnah to complete the wash.
If these are not removed, the wudu may be incomplete.

Source Text

ووضعه التجفيف وإن مسح لا يبالغ فيه وأن تكون آنيته من خزف، وغسل عروتها ثلاثاً، على يساره ووضع اليد حالة الغسل على عروته لا رأسه وتعاهد موقيه وما تحت الخاتم، ومجاوزة حدود الفروض إطالة للغرة وملء آنيته استعداداً لوقت آخر، وقراءة سورة القدر ثلاثاً لقوله : من قرأ في أثر وضوئه إنا أنزلناه في ليلة القدر مرة واحدة كان من الصديقين ومن قرأها مرتين كتب في ديوان الشهداء ومن قرأها ثلاثاً . حشره الله الأنبياء أخرجه الديلمي، ولما ذكره الفقيه أبو الليث في مقدمته . بالثوب قال : لا بأس به قاله محمد و به نأخذ ولا نرى بذلك بأساً، وهو قول أبي حنيفة : اهـ وفي الحانية لا بأس للمتوضىء، والمغتسل أن يتمسح بالمنديل روي عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه كان يفعل ذلك، وهو الصحيح إلا أنه ينبغي أن لا يبالغ ولا يستقصي فيبقى أثر الوضوء على الأعضاء اهـ. ملخصاً، ووردت عدة أحاديث على أنه فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام، وهذا كله إذا لم يكن حاجة إلى التنشيف فإن كانت فالظاهر أنه لا يختلف في جوازه من غير كراهة، بل في استحبابه، أو وجوبه بحسب تلك الحاجة العارضة المندفعة به. قاله ابن أمير حاج : ثم قال : وهذا في الحي، أما الميت فمقتضى كلام مشايخنا أنه مستحب لئلا تبتل أكفانه فيصير مثله اهـ . قوله : (وإن تكون آنيته من خزف فإنه روي أن الملائكة تزور بيت من آنیته . من خزف من المسلمين قوله : (وغسل عروتها (ثلاثاً) ليتيقن الطهارة . قوله : ( ووضعه على يساره) ليصب منه على يمينه، وتقدم له ما يفيد ذلك قوله: (لا رأسه تحامياً عن تقاطر الماء المستعمل، وقوله : حالة الغسل أي حالة إرادة الصب للغسل ولا يظهر حال الغسل الحقيقي لأن اليدين مشغولتان بغسل الأعضاء قوله : (وما تحت الخاتم تقدم ما يفيده قوله : (إطالة للغرة) المراد بها ما يعم التحجيل، وإطالة الغرة تكون بالزيادة على الحد المحدود كما في البحر، وأما التحجيل فقال في شرح الشرعة : إنّه يغسل الذراعين لنصف العضدين، والرجلين لنصف الساقين اهـ. قوله: استعداداً لوقت (آخر) لو قال لوضوء آخر لكان أولى ليعم الوضوء على الوضوء في وقت واحد قوله : ( لقوله الله الخ) أخرجه الديلمي في مسند Exceeding Obligatory Limits (Ghurrah and Tahjil) and Recitation of Surat al-Qadr
Definition of ghurrah/tahjil and recommendation of reciting Surat al-Qadr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meaning of ghurrah and tahjil in wudu and state the recommendation of reciting Surat al-Qadr after wudu, including the evidence and its authenticity.

Core Idea
Ghurrah and tahjil mean washing beyond the obligations (to upper arms and calves); reciting Surat al-Qadr three times after wudu brings great reward, though the hadith is weak.

This lesson covers two additional recommended acts: extending the wash beyond the obligatory parts to achieve the 'blaze' (ghurrah) and 'white feet' (tahjil), and reciting Surat al-Qadr after wudu. The text defines ghurrah as washing the forearms up to half the upper arms and the feet up to half the calves. The recitation is supported by a hadith from al-Daylami, but the commentator notes its weakness.

Guided Path
1
Define ghurrah and tahjil
Ghurrah (blaze) refers to the radiant mark from washing beyond the obligatory parts; tahjil is the white on the feet from washing up to half the calves.
These are metaphorical terms for the extra washing.
2
Identify the extent of the extra wash
For ghurrah and tahjil, one washes the forearms up to half the upper arms, and the feet up to half the calves.
This is the definition from Sharh al-Shir'a as cited in the text.
3
Understand the purpose
The purpose is to lengthen the 'blaze' by increasing beyond the limit, as a sunnah for beautification and reward.
This is recommended, not obligatory.
4
Recite Surat al-Qadr after wudu
Reciting Surat al-Qadr three times after wudu is recommended due to a hadith promising great reward.
The hadith is weak according to al-Maqasid al-Hasana.
5
Evaluate the hadith's authenticity
The commentator notes that al-Daylami reported it, but later scholars like al-Sakhawi deem it baseless.
Despite weakness, the practice is encouraged by some Hanafi scholars due to the meaning.

الفردوس، قوله: (كتب في ديوان الشهداء الديوان بالكسر ويفتح مجمع الصحف، والكتاب يكتب فيه أهل الجيش، وأهل العطية، وأوّل من وضعه عمر رضي الله عنه قاموس فالمراد أنه يكتب اسمه مع أسمائهم في محل كتابتهم، والمراد منه ومما قبله أن يعطي ثوابهم وإن تفاوتت الكيفيات. قوله: (حشره الله محشر (الأنبياء بكسر الشين وتفتح محل الإجتماع أي، وإذا إجتمع معهم في مجمعهم لا يضام لأن مصاحب الكرام لا يضام . قوله: (ولما ذكره الفقيه أبو الليث في مقدمته ذكره المصنف في كبيره قال في المقاصد الحسنة : حديث قراءة إنا أنزلناه عقب الوضوء لا أصل له انتهى ويعني به ما ذكر في المقدمة ولفظه يدل على وضعه.
And drying with a cloth, even if wiping, do not exaggerate. And that his vessel be of clay. And washing its handle three times, and placing it on his left, and placing the hand during washing on its handle, not its head. And tending to his watch-straps and what is under the ring. And exceeding the limits of the obligatory acts to lengthen the blaze (al-ghurrah) and filling his vessel in preparation for another time. And reciting Surat al-Qadr three times due to his saying: Whoever recites after his wudu 'Inna anzalnahu fi laylat al-qadr' once will be among the truthful, and whoever recites it twice will be recorded in the register of martyrs, and whoever recites it three times, Allah will gather him in the gathering-place of the prophets. Reported by al-Daylami, and as mentioned by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth in his introduction. By a cloth: He said: there is no harm in it, said by Muhammad, and we adopt it and see no harm in that, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa. End. And in al-Haniyya: There is no harm for the one performing wudu or ghusl to wipe with a handkerchief; it is reported from the Messenger of Allah that he used to do that, and it is correct, except that one should not exaggerate nor seek to remove all traces, leaving some effect of wudu on the limbs. End. Summarized. And several hadiths have been reported that he did that. All this if there is no need for drying; if there is need, then apparently there is no disagreement about its permissibility without dislike, rather it is recommended or obligatory depending on that incidental need that is repelled by it. Ibn Amir Haj said: Then he said: This is for the living; as for the dead, the implication of the words of our shaykhs is that it is recommended so that his shrouds do not become wet and thus become like him. End. His saying: (and that his vessel be of clay) because it is reported that the angels visit the house of a Muslim whose vessel is of clay. His saying: (and washing its handle three times) to be certain of purity. His saying: (and placing it on his left) so that he pours from it onto his right, and it preceded that which indicates this. His saying: (not its head) to avoid dripping of used water. And his saying: (state of washing) meaning the state of intending to pour for washing, and it is not apparent in the actual state of washing because the hands are busy washing the limbs. His saying: (and what is under the ring) preceded that which indicates it. His saying: (to lengthen the blaze (al-ghurrah)) meaning that which includes the tahjil, and lengthening the ghurrah is by increasing beyond the defined limit as in al-Bahr. As for al-tahjil, he said in Sharh al-Shir'a: That he washes the forearms up to half of the upper arms, and the feet up to half of the calves. End. His saying: (in preparation for another time) it would have been better if he said 'for another wudu' to include wudu upon wudu at one time. His saying: (due to his saying) reported by al-Daylami in Musnad al-Firdaws. His saying: (recorded in the register of martyrs) al-diwan (with kasr and fatah) is the collection of scrolls, and the book in which the army and those receiving stipends are recorded, and the first to establish it was Umar. So the meaning is that his name is written with their names in their writing place. And the intended meaning from this and what preceded is that he is given their reward even if the qualities differ. His saying: (Allah will gather him in the gathering-place of the prophets) with kasr of the shin and fat-h as the place of gathering; i.e., when he gathers with them in their gathering place, he will not be harmed because the companion of noble ones is not harmed. His saying: (and as mentioned by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth in his introduction) the author mentioned it in his big book. He said in al-Maqasid al-Hasana: The hadith of reciting 'Inna anzalnahu' after wudu has no basis, meaning what was mentioned in the introduction, and its wording indicates its fabrication.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiyah) on the recommended acts (adab) of wudu as outlined in Maraqi al-Falah. The commentator expands on each act, providing proofs and clarifications. The first act is drying with a cloth after wudu: it is permissible, not disliked, as adopted from Muhammad and Abu Hanifa. However, exaggeration in drying is discouraged to leave some trace of wudu. If there is a need (e.g., cold weather), it becomes recommended or even obligatory. For the deceased, drying is recommended to avoid wetting the shroud. Second, the vessel should be of clay because angels visit such homes. Third, the handle should be washed three times to ensure purity. Fourth, the vessel should be placed on the left hand so that water may be poured with the right. Fifth, during washing, one should hold the handle, not the head, to avoid drips of used water. Sixth, one should attend to watch-straps and under the ring to ensure water reaches those areas. Seventh, one should exceed the obligatory limits by washing beyond the elbows and ankles to achieve the 'blaze' (ghurrah) and 'tahjil'—the latter meaning washing half the upper arms and half the calves. Eighth, filling the vessel in advance for another wudu is recommended, even for consecutive wudus. Ninth, reciting Surat al-Qadr three times after wudu brings great reward, though the hadith is considered weak by some scholars. The commentator discusses the hadith's authenticity, noting that al-Daylami reported it but al-Maqasid al-Hasana deems it baseless. Overall, these acts are sunnah, not obligatory, but performing them earns reward and perfection in worship.

Key Terms
غرة (ghurrah): The white blaze; metaphor for washing beyond obligation on arms
تحجيل (tahjil): Washing the feet up to half the calves

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the sunnah extent for tahjil?
A) Washing up to the knees
B) Washing up to half the calves
C) Washing the feet only
D) No specific extent

Key Takeaway
Ghurrah and tahjil are sunnah acts of extending the wash, while reciting Surat al-Qadr after wudu is a recommended practice based on a weak hadith.
